Educational News

Important News

The Ministry of Education Pays Attention to Overseas Chinese Education 87

▲Appealing Again for Overseas Chinese Education in Taiwan

Regarding the case of Japanese interference in overseas Chinese education in Taiwan, the Ministry of Education had previously consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the Japanese government, based on the petition submitted by representatives of Taiwanese public organizations. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs replied that it would wait for the establishment of a consulate to handle the matter. The Ministry of Education believed that this was not urgent and consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs again, stating that regarding the case of Japanese interference in overseas Chinese education in Taiwan, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had already replied to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Association that the establishment of a consulate had been scheduled for Taiwan and that it would be easier to handle the matter on-site after the consulate was established. The Ministry of Education considered that the number of overseas Chinese schools in Taiwan was limited and that it would be acceptable to wait for the establishment of a consulate before handling the matter on-site. However, the Ministry's intention was: (1) the local overseas Chinese publicly expressed their concerns about this case and traveled thousands of miles back to China to petition, indicating that the situation was very urgent. If it were to wait for the establishment of a consulate before handling the matter on-site, it was feared that it would be too late; (2) the governments of various British and Dutch colonies had interfered with overseas Chinese education, and the Chinese government had repeatedly ordered local consuls to negotiate earnestly with the governments of the places of residence, but all had failed to achieve satisfactory results. If the responsibility for handling this case were again assigned to the consuls, it was feared that it would still not produce results in the future; (3) there were thousands of overseas Chinese schools, and except for those in American territories, they were all under the pressure of powerful forces. Millions of overseas Chinese were hoping to restore freedom through Chinese sovereignty. If this case could be traded for victory, the impact would only be fortunate for a few overseas Chinese schools in Taiwan; (4) there were many schools established by Japanese expatriates in mainland China, and China did not interfere with them, while Japan interfered with Chinese schools in Taiwan, which violated the principle of equality and reciprocity. If Japan did not change its mind, China could follow suit. For the sake of the schools established by Japan, they would not insist on not allowing it. Based on the above reasons, it is proposed that the previous consultation be followed to emphasize education and suppress the expectations of overseas Chinese.

▲Instructing to Maintain Overseas Chinese Education in the Philippines

The Ministry of Education instructed the Consul General stationed in the Philippines to work with the Philippine Overseas Chinese Education Association and the Chamber of Commerce to find ways to maintain the educational surcharge and to raise long-term funding for education. It stated that, according to the Philippine Chinese newspapers, some Chinese merchants in the area were not paying the educational surcharge on time, resulting in a shortfall of more than 40,000 yuan in the funds for March to May of this year, causing an economic panic in overseas Chinese education. The Board of Directors of the Overseas Chinese Education Association has now resolved three remedial measures: (1) From February to the end of May of this year, the monthly salaries of teachers and staff in each school will be reduced by 20%. The monthly salary of teachers and staff in public schools is more than 11,000 yuan, and a 20% reduction would be approximately 2,205 yuan, totaling 8,820 yuan for four months. (2) Students in each primary school will donate 2 yuan per student, and students in each middle school will donate 4 yuan per student, which is expected to raise approximately 5,000 yuan. (3) The Board of Directors of the Overseas Chinese Education Association will separately solicit special donations from the overseas Chinese community. The Ministry of Education considers that the overseas Chinese in the Philippines have always been enthusiastic about education, and the educational surcharge system they created is a model for overseas Chinese in other places. The central government is planning to issue a general order to overseas Chinese in various ports to emulate it. Recently, due to the existence of some hesitant donors, the donations have suddenly become scarce, which is a great concern. The measures proposed by the Overseas Chinese Education Association can alleviate the situation temporarily. However, the salaries of teachers and staff in overseas Chinese schools in the Philippines are not high to begin with. Reducing them further will make it difficult to maintain a livelihood. Students already bear a heavy burden by paying tuition fees annually, and collecting donations will be too much for the poor to bear. As for soliciting special donations, although there will be no shortage of generous people, it is not a long-term solution. Overseas Chinese education in the Philippines has a history of 30 years, and its relationship to the future of the overseas Chinese community is particularly important. In recent years, the overseas Chinese business has gradually declined, and the way to save it depends on education. The overseas Chinese business pays a small annual surcharge to maintain its glorious history and save its difficult future, which is worth doing. A small number of overseas Chinese businesses may occasionally err in their understanding of this meaning, trying to save a small amount of money without considering the long-term benefits, or it may be a temporary mistake. The consul, together with the directors of the Overseas Chinese Education Association and the various levels of the Overseas Chinese Chamber of Commerce, should earnestly persuade and guide them, so that those who have not paid will pay quickly, and those who do not pay will resume paying. The surcharge can be maintained, and education will not decline. If there is a long-term solution to increase funding, it should also be considered to supplement and remedy the situation and seek development. The overseas Chinese businesses in the Philippines are known for their public spirit, and it is hoped that they will all understand this meaning, work hard, and not be negligent.

Graduation and Enrollment Examinations Require Supervision

Both examinations are very important. Dr. Ma Guli 94

Lectures at Shanghai College of Law and Politics

Dr. Ma Guli, a special commissioner sent by the French Ministry of Education to China to investigate higher education and to promote cultural exchange between China and the West, has been welcomed by the Chinese education community. The other day, at the invitation of Dr. Zheng Yuxiu, president of the Shanghai College of Law and Politics, Mr. Ma gave a lecture at the school. The meeting started at 4:00 pm. First, Dr. Zhu Foding, the dean of academic affairs, gave a speech and introduced Dr. Ma. Then Mr. Ma took the stage and delivered a lecture in Chinese on the topic of "An Overview of Sino-Western Cultural Exchange." His Chinese pronunciation was clear and fluent, even surpassing that of southern Chinese speakers of Beijing dialect. Finally, Principal Zheng of the school gave a thank-you speech and a photo was taken to commemorate the occasion. Mr. Ma is proficient in more than a dozen languages and this is his first visit to China. He usually enjoys studying Chinese literature and writing articles. He now plans to establish an organization for the exchange of Chinese and French culture with well-known figures such as Li Shizeng, Cai Yuanpei, Wu Zhihui, and Principal Zheng of the school, to carry out general publicity between the two countries.

Results of Shanghai County Sports Meet 105

▲The First Joint Primary School Sports Meet and the Second Amateur Sports Meet

The first Shanghai County Joint Primary School Sports Meet and the second Amateur Sports Meet were held in Minhang the other day. On the second day, it suddenly rained heavily. The organizing committee held the track and field events in the rain because it was inconvenient for various groups from afar to travel back and forth. The Shanghai-Minhang Motor Road was used as a running track, and the track and field venue was muddy. Staff members worked together to drain the accumulated water from the venue and cover it with fine sand. In the afternoon, the weather suddenly cleared up, and the events were able to continue. However, all the events did not end until 7:30 pm. Scores were tallied, prizes were awarded, and the meeting adjourned, after 9:00 pm. At the moment, the two events of tennis and soccer have not been played due to rain. It is said that they will be convened again on a scheduled date. Wuxi Amateur Tennis Competition 107

▲Registration Deadline on the 12th

The second amateur tennis competition organized by the Wuxi Public Sports Field has received enthusiastic registration since the announcement of the regulations. As of yesterday, more than 50 people have registered, especially beginners. Before 9:00 a.m. and after 4:00 p.m. every day, people bring tennis rackets to the field for practice in an endless stream. In order to facilitate the observation of members' levels and fair grouping, the field has specially divided members and non-members for practice. The original three tennis courts are surrounded by high fences for members to use. In addition, three new tennis courts have been set up in the south of the football field, separated by bamboo screens, for non-members to practice. It is said that the registration deadline is on the 12th of this month. In this week, many more players will definitely register.

Anhui Province Organizes Sports Promotion Association 109

Li Shaoling, Inspector of the Anhui Education Department, Wu Zhongjun and Geng Bowei, physical education teachers at Anhui University, Yao Changlin and Li Kehang, physical education teachers at Anhui No. 1 Middle School, etc., deeply stimulated by the repeated failures of Anhui Province's various sports in the Huazhong Games and the National Games, initiated the organization of a provincial sports promotion association, hoping to break the past dull atmosphere and arouse the attention of people throughout the province. Since its initiation, advanced figures in the sports world and those with aspirations for sports have expressed their support and joined the association. Yesterday, the 23rd, the initiators held the first meeting at the Public Sports Field, attended by Li Heling, Wu Zhongjun, Geng Bowei, Li Kehang, Xie Peisan, Yao Changlin, Jin Shisheng, Qi Yuetan, Hu Shuzu, and more than ten others. Despite the heavy rain, the initiators were extremely excited and discussed proposals for as long as four hours. Finally, Li Shaoling, Wu Zhongjun, Jin Shisheng, Li Kehang, and Geng Bowei were elected as preparatory committee members to prepare for the convening of the general meeting. Wu Zhongjun and Jin Shisheng were appointed as drafters to draft the constitution of the general meeting. It was decided to divide the association into two major groups, schools and society, to ensure that public sports and school sports develop equally. It is said that various agencies and schools in Anhui will enthusiastically support the association.

Customs Implemented 111

Prohibition of Silver Ingot Imports

In order to alleviate the silver price, the Ministry of Finance has issued an order to all customs offices to prohibit the import of Mexican silver dollars as a temporary measure to address the symptoms. The Jianghai Customs also received the above order yesterday and immediately implemented the prohibition of silver ingot imports.

French Consulate Not Easy 112

To Endorse Chinese Passports

Requires a 500 Yuan Guarantee Before Endorsing

Our Country's Diplomatic Authorities Are Negotiating

The French Consulate General in Shanghai requires Chinese citizens applying for passports to France for business to pay a cash deposit of 500 yuan as a guarantee before endorsing the passport. For those traveling to countries such as Portugal and Belgium via France, a bank guarantee is also required for endorsement. Recently, it has been heard that the French Consulate General requires Chinese citizens applying for passports to France or traveling to countries such as Portugal and Belgium for business or travel to submit a deposit of 500 yuan per person before endorsing the passport. This measure violates international practice. Our country's diplomatic authorities have made informal inquiries to the French Consulate as to why this new regulation was not notified to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and demanded a change. Negotiations are currently underway.

Local 113

Anti-British Movement by Indians

An Indian Detained for Distributing Leaflets

Wenhui Bao reported that this morning (7th), an Indian named Ye Jiaxin was charged in the British Police Court with spreading seditious writings. The defendant did not hire a lawyer. The police were represented by lawyer Winter, who claimed that at 0:15 this morning, Western policeman Hull noticed three Indians on Wusong Road holding leaflets and putting them into residents' houses. After observing for a while, he followed them secretly, hoping to persuade other policemen to capture all three. However, the Indians noticed and immediately ran away. He chased and caught one person, who is the defendant in this case. The leaflets were in English and stated, in brief, that Indians are no longer loyal subjects of the United Kingdom. Indians residing in Shanghai and its vicinity hereby declare that they are no longer British citizens. This is because the Indian government has created a political storm and an era of terror, forcing them to carry two hearts. Today, under the leadership of Gandhi in India, a policy of non-violent resistance is being vigorously implemented. It has now been extended to the Indians in Shanghai, who unanimously denounce the registration regulations of the British Consulate General and will no longer register, but will begin to adopt a policy of non-violent resistance. They earnestly hope that the Chinese government will consider the goodwill between the Chinese and Indian peoples, provide assistance, and show sympathy. The court immediately announced an adjournment for 14 days for continued hearing. The defendant was remanded in custody, and the police were ordered to arrest the other two Indians and bring them to justice.

Understanding and Efforts to Commemorate the National Humiliation of May 9th 114

May 9th is the anniversary of the national humiliation fifteen years ago when Japanese imperialism, taking advantage of the heat of the European War, forced the then Beijing puppet government to sign the Twenty-One Demands, which could lead to national subjugation and extinction. The Twenty-One Demands included five items: first, to plunder the rights of transfer of ports, railways, mines, and leased territories that Germany had previously seized within Shandong; second, to actively annex Manchuria and Mongolia; third, to seize the right to dispose of the Hanyeping Company's assets and the right to mine nearby; fourth, to encompass all ports and islands along our coast; and fifth, to plunder important domestic affairs such as our national military, police, finance, transportation, and culture. The illegal proposal of the Twenty-One Demands and forced recognition have no basis in law. However, repeated requests to the Paris Peace Conference and the Washington Conference to adjudicate and cancel the demands have not been achieved, which shows that imperialists only know how to divide the spoils and do not know the truth. To avenge the national humiliation, we must endure hardship and strive for self-improvement. Yuan Shikai sought help from Japan to establish an imperial system, not hesitating to cede power and humiliate the country by signing the Twenty-One Demands. This time, the Yan-Feng rebel party also did not hesitate to collude with imperialism and betray the country for personal gain. Therefore, to commemorate the national humiliation of May 9th, we must support the central government, eliminate the rebels, and ensure that there are no more warlords who betray the country. For more than fifty years, Japan's aggression against China has become increasingly urgent. In recent years, it has been particularly active in managing Manchuria and Mongolia. To commemorate the national humiliation of May 9th, we must effectively abolish unequal treaties to remove their guarantee. We must vigorously promote the national goods movement to resist their economic aggression. We must actively develop manpower and financial resources towards Manchuria and Mongolia to eliminate their ambitions in the region.

Slogans: (1) The Twenty-One Demands are Japan's concrete plan to destroy China. (2) Yuan Shikai is the culprit who betrayed the Republic of China and forfeited national rights. (3) Only by eliminating domestic warlords can we overthrow all imperialism. (4) Only by vigorously promoting revolutionary construction can we abolish unequal treaties. (5) To commemorate May 9th, we must eliminate counter-revolutionary forces. (6) To commemorate May 9th, we must eliminate the remaining warlords who betrayed the country, Yan Xishan and Feng Yuxiang. (7) To commemorate May 9th, we must promote national goods and resist Japanese economic aggression. (8) To commemorate May 9th, we must support the central government and consolidate unity. (9) Down with Japanese imperialism! (10) Support the Chinese Kuomintang!

Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters of the Chinese Kuomintang

Rice and Grain 115

Minutes of the Second Standing Committee Meeting of the Fair Price Association

Fair Prices to Be Held from May 10th

The Municipal Rice and Grain Fair Price Committee held its second standing committee meeting the day before yesterday afternoon at 2:00 p.m. The attendees were Yao Zirang, Yan Xiaoquan, Wang Boxun, Wang Yiting, Tang Naikang (representing Xu Shaoxiu), Zhu Zixiang, Xu Fu (representing Xu Yang), Ye Huijun, Weng Yinchu, Huang Hanzhi, Sun Yishan, Yuan Liang (representing Shen Zengyuan), Mo Zijing, Qin Yanqi, Pan Gongzhan, Gu Xinyi, Lin Kanghou, and Lu Wenshao. The meeting was chaired by Committee Member Pan Gongzhan. The agenda included: (1) Chairman's report: (A) Quantity of rice to be determined. According to the procurement department, as of April 24th, a total of 1,500 bags of Jiaojiao rice in stock, 500 bags of Mindang rice, and 3,028 bags of Saigon No. 2 rice have been ordered, all priced at 15 yuan per stone. In addition, 500 bags of Mindang rice have been ordered at a price of 14 yuan and 95 cents per stone. The futures of 50,000 bags of Xiaojiao rice for May are 7 taels and 1 qian and 7 fen per dan, which is approximately 14 yuan and 93 cents per stone. (B) Matters concerning advance payments. The first batch of more than 5,000 bags of rice has been arranged by the chairman to be paid in advance by the General Manager of the Shanghai Municipal Bank. As for the advance payment matters for subsequent shipments, it is proposed that Committee Members Xu, Lin, and Wang jointly discuss and form another banking group to handle them. (C) The Municipal Government's fair price rice funds have been submitted to the Mayor by the association, urging the Finance Bureau to allocate them in advance to facilitate the progress. (D) The Qianye Guild has nominated Mr. Wang Boxun as a member of the association and has submitted a request to the Mayor for additional appointment. (E) In order to reduce the cost of fair price rice, a letter has been sent to the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, requesting that all import taxes and duties on fair price rice be exempted as an example. (2) Committee Member Ye Huijun reported that (A) the Commercial Association has convened a meeting yesterday to discuss the matter of soliciting donations. How to allocate the 30,000 yuan donation among various industries has not yet been decided, but in any case, the full amount should be raised. It is currently being actively carried out. (B) The Bean and Rice Guild has also convened a meeting of its members to discuss the issue of fair price rice sales. If the rice is sold at the purchase price of 15 yuan, it may not be in line with public opinion and will lose the meaning of fair price. It is best to sell it at 14 yuan, or at most 14 yuan and 50 cents. As for the deficit, if it is considered too large and cannot be raised, the guild may be able to add another 10,000 yuan on top of the previously recognized 10,000 yuan. (3) Committee Member Lu Wenshao reported that (A) the fair price rice is scheduled to be held on May 1st. At present, the deadline is approaching urgently. If it is held in all places at the same time, it may not be feasible in practice, or it may be held in a few places first. (B) The staff of each fair price point should be hired with funds to take responsibility. The salary is about 20 yuan per month with meals and about 30 yuan per month without meals. Matters for discussion: (A) Please discuss and decide on the date and price of the fair price rice. (Chairman's temporary motion) Resolved: (1) Date issue. Since the locations and equipment of each fair price point have not yet been arranged properly, it is too urgent to hold it on May 1st. It is resolved to postpone it for ten days and set the date for all points to open simultaneously on May 10th. (2) Price issue. Since the market price fluctuates greatly, a meeting should be convened again before the opening to decide. (B) The case of forming another banking group to handle the advance payment for the rice to be ordered (proposed by the chairman) was resolved. (1) Please invite the Municipal Bank to jointly organize an advance payment banking group with the silver and money industries, to be convened by Committee Member Xu. (2) Send a letter to large organizations as soon as possible, urging them to deliver the donations to the Municipal Bank immediately, and set May 5th as the deadline for raising the full amount of donations. (C) How to plan, supervise, and promote the fair price rice in rural areas (proposed by the chairman) was resolved. The Social Bureau should convene municipal council members from various districts for discussion and then determine the method. Committee Member Lu Wenshao is also invited to participate in the discussion at the meeting. (D) The proposal to change the appointment of Committee Member Sun Yishan as a member of the distribution department and request additional ratification (proposed by the chairman) was passed. (E) Please decide on the location of the sales points for fair price rice in the urban area (proposed by the chairman). (F) Opinion on handling the fair price rice point proposed by Committee Member Sun Yishan. (G) A proposal to formulate methods and opinions for distributing fair price rice (proposed by Committee Member Lu Wenshao). The above three cases were discussed together. (Resolution) (1) The locations of the nine distribution points for fair price rice in the urban area are tentatively set as (A) Jinling Guild Hall in the new western district, (B) Charity Group in the southern city, (C) Chaozhou Guild Hall at the Southern Railway Station, (D) Yangshupu in the eastern Shanghai, (E) Xiahai Temple, (F) Caojiadu in the western Shanghai, (G) Lannidu in Pudong, (H) Charity Group and Congee Factory in Zhabei, (I) Zhabei (location not yet determined). The locations of the above points will be determined after investigation by the members of the distribution department. (2) The staff of each distribution point will be fully selected and assigned by the members of the distribution department, with eight people as the standard for each point, distributed as follows: one director/accountant, two managers, three rice measurers, and two warehouse keepers. (3) The rice and grain for distribution will be directly delivered to each distribution point by the procurement department for weighing and unloading. The legitimate loss of rice quantity during shipment and transportation shall not exceed one pound per bag. If there is an excess, the carrier shall be responsible. (4) Rice purchase coupons will be divided into two types, one sheng and five sheng. (5) Each household can purchase a maximum of five sheng of rice. (6) The rice selling hours are set from 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and from 2:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. daily. (7) All methods for preventing fraud and other matters at each point will be formulated by the members of the distribution department and submitted to the chairman for decision. (8) A letter will be sent to Wang Xiaolai, Huang Jinrong, Du Yuesheng, and Zhang Xiaolin, requesting them to donate funds and initiate fundraising performances (temporary motion by Committee Member Ye). (Resolution) Committee Member Ye will first contact Mr. Wang Xiaolai and then send a letter. (9) To appoint two responsible committee members from each department to facilitate communication (temporary motion by the chairman). (Resolution) Xu Fu and Pan Gongzhan are appointed as responsible committee members for the economic department, Zhu Zixiang and Yan Xiaoquan are appointed as responsible committee members for the procurement department, and Lu Wenshao and Sun Yishan are appointed as responsible committee members for the distribution department. (10) To decide on the date of the next standing committee meeting (Resolution) To be convened temporarily by the chairman.

Chu Minyi Attends 116

International Child Welfare Association

To be Held in Belgium in June and July This Year

The Third International Exhibition of Child Welfare is scheduled to be held in Beijing from June 27th to July 7th this year. The Chinese government approved the notes from the Belgian Embassy in China, requesting the dispatch of personnel to participate in the meeting. The Ministry of Health and Education, considering that Chinese Committee Member Chu Minyi will be going to Belgium to participate in the World Expo, and that Chu's knowledge and reputation are respected both at home and abroad, specially appointed Chu as the representative of the Ministry of Health and Education of the Republic of China to attend the meeting. The letter from the ministry to Chu is recorded as follows: "According to the official letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Third International Exhibition of Child Welfare is scheduled to be held in Beijing from June 27th to July 7th, 1930. The Belgian Minister in China has requested the dispatch of personnel to participate in the meeting, instructing us to investigate and respond. It is found that since our country has been invited to this exhibition, we should send personnel to attend. Mr. Chu has excellent academic reputation and is highly respected at home and abroad. He has been researching health education theories and developing national sports. Now, in view of the centenary of Belgian independence, the Chinese Education Museum is holding an exhibition in Belgium. We plan to ask you to go nearby as a representative to attend the meeting, to promote international friendship. Attached is a letter of appointment. Please check and receive it. We hope that you will report the situation of the meeting and the attendance at any time. Liu Ruiheng and Jiang Menglin respectfully inform you. The letter is said to have been sent to Mr. Chu by the Secretariat of the Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee.

The Ministry of Communications Rectifies Shanghai's Telephone System 125

Adopts Suggestions from the Public Utilities Bureau

The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, recognizing that telephones are a crucial municipal facility closely linked to the development of municipal industries, the maintenance of public safety, and the improvement of municipal transportation, and noting that there are many aspects of the city's telephone system that require rectification and improvement, previously drafted ten suggestions for rectification and submitted them to the Municipal Government for forwarding to the Ministry of Communications for review. As reported earlier, the Ministry has now responded to the Municipal Government, indicating its adoption of the suggestions put forward by the Public Utilities Bureau. A summary is provided below: (1) Regarding amending the business charter and expanding the scope of operations, the Ministry stated that the scope of telephone operations is determined by the development of the city. In rural areas outside the scope, fees should be determined by the distance of the line. However, the public may be unable to afford installation due to excessive fees. The Shanghai Telephone Bureau should be instructed to closely observe the development trends of the city at any time, consider expanding the scope of operations, and properly revise the fee regulations. (2) Regarding changing or canceling the charging method for Chinese-foreign calls, the Ministry stated that a call contract was signed between the Shanghai Telephone Bureau and Chinese-foreign companies in December 1925, and the charging method was clearly stipulated. Now that this contract is about to expire, the Bureau should be instructed to negotiate with the company to improve it as much as possible when renewing the contract. (3) Regarding the installation of public telephones, the Ministry believes that it is indeed essential and immediately instructs the Telephone Bureau to consider the situation and widely install them. (4) Regarding the recovery of the Songyang Telephone Company, the Ministry stated that it had previously instructed the Bureau to properly draft a recovery plan and should now urge it to proceed effectively. (5) Regarding the Pudong Branch, the Ministry has decided to establish it, and the required machinery and line materials have been ordered from the United States. The land has been purchased and is ready for the construction of the bureau building. (6) Regarding the widespread establishment of branch offices, it concerns technical and economic research and should be instructed to inform the Telephone Bureau of this for reference. The new West District Branch has now been fully installed and will soon be in operation. (7) Regarding the addition of relay lines, the relay lines between Nanshi and Zhabei were originally rented by the Telephone Bureau from Chinese-foreign companies. Now that they are insufficient, dozens of pairs have been added and are being negotiated. Regarding the relay lines between various bureaus and the concessions, the Bureau has been instructed to ascertain the required situation and consider increasing them. (8) Regarding the rectification of lines, the Ministry stated that although Shanghai's telephone lines are rectified from time to time, the occurrence of faults is still inevitable and should be strictly inspected by the Bureau to achieve perfection. (9) Regarding the recovery of Chinese and foreign telephones, the Ministry stated that it has instructed the Shanghai Telephone Bureau to prepare to lay lines for negotiation and should urge it to expedite the process. To restore sovereignty, it is planned to nationalize all Shanghai telephones, and efforts are being made to actively pursue this. (10) Regarding the banning and recovery of foreign telephone lines on both sides of roads built beyond boundaries, the Ministry agreed to instruct the Bureau to ascertain the number of households, ban and recover them. As mentioned above, the Ministry of Communications has strictly instructed the Shanghai Telephone Bureau, which is directly under its jurisdiction, to handle the improvement of Shanghai's telephone system item by item and effectively. The Bureau has the responsibility to refresh the telephone system and increase convenience and should strive to carry it out to live up to the expectations of the entire citizenry.

Shipping News 126

Additional New Vessels on the Tongyang Route.

The route from Shanghai to Tongyang, commonly known as the Little Yangtze River, sees a huge amount of annual cargo transportation. In particular, cotton, native cloth, and livestock such as pigs, sheep, ducks, and geese are transported to Shanghai in large quantities. Initially, only the Dada Company operated five ships on this route. Later, the Datong Company followed, and to this day, there are also four ships from Hongda, Longda, and Zhengda companies plying the route. Recently, with ships going up and down the Yangtze River calling at Tongyang, more cargo and passengers are coming and going. The Shanghai-based, Chinese-owned Minxing Shipping Company has also been established and is operating a dedicated Tongyang service, assigning two ships. One is named Hanping, which will start its first voyage today. The other, named Xiechang, is a newly built vessel. The hull has been completed, and the passenger cabins are currently being installed. It will also be able to set sail soon.

Headquarters Investigates Commercial Vessels

The Transportation Department of the Headquarters issued a notice to various shipping companies yesterday, stating that the department is responsible for managing transportation and has the responsibility to investigate Chinese commercial vessels. A survey form is hereby stipulated and attached to the document. It is hoped that various shipping companies will fill it out and report back by the deadline. The form includes items such as the name of the ship, tonnage, length, passenger cabins, cargo space, engine, boiler, speed, and the year of construction, as well as the current route. The various companies are currently complying and submitting the forms.

Kuaili Ordered to Be Returned to the China Merchants Bureau

The Kuaili ship of the China Merchants Bureau's Upper Yangtze River fleet has been out of service for more than a year. It has now been ordered to be returned to Shanghai by the Shipping Department. The bureau received a telegram yesterday stating that the ship could enter the port today. After arriving in Shanghai, it must be repaired and sent to Yichang to resume operations. Currently, only the Jiangtian and Jiangyu ships of the bureau's Yangtze River fleet have not resumed service.

Wenzhou Martial Law Delays Ships

Yesterday, various shipping agencies in Shanghai received telegrams from Wenzhou stating that Wenzhou had declared special martial law since May 4th, prohibiting ships from traveling at night. Therefore, ships arriving in Wenzhou after 6 PM could only anchor outside the port, and night work was prohibited at the docks. As a result, all ships on the Wenzhou route to Shanghai have been delayed. Passengers arriving in Wenzhou are being subjected to stricter inspections.

Ship Rentals Have Been Collected

Last year, the ships rented by the Transportation Department of the Headquarters for the suppression of rebellion still had outstanding payments for tolls, coal, etc., in addition to the rent that had already been paid. The management office has now received a special telegram instructing the Shanghai shipping agencies to send personnel with a list of rental dates to Beijing to collect the outstanding payments. Yesterday, the various companies sent personnel to Beijing and collected the full amount of the ship rentals.

News of the Youth Asia Walking Group 127

Actively Preparing

The Chinese Youth Asia Walking Group, initiated by overseas Chinese Feng Binghun and Li Mengsheng from Fujian and Guangdong, has recruited more than twenty young men and women comrades after two weeks of effort and established a temporary office at 218 Dongbaoxing Road for contact purposes. It is reported that the comrades participating in the group are mostly children of overseas Chinese who have been engaged in revolutionary work for many years, as well as famous local literary and art writers. The group has convened the first and second discussion meetings and decided that the first phase of the route will start from Shanghai, pass through the capital, go west along the Yangtze River, pass through Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan, and end in Chengdu, Sichuan, as the end point of the first phase. Then, the organization will be expanded, and equipment will be added to start moving towards western Sichuan and Qinghai, tracing the Jinsha River, exploring the source of the river, climbing the Kunlun Mountains, passing through the Gansu-Xinjiang border, to reach the Pamirs, and passing through Near East Afghanistan, Persia, Turkey, and other countries, and then return home, passing through India, Burma, towards Siam and Indochina, etc., to implement its second and third phases of grand aspirations. It is also reported that all the purchase expenses of the group are borne by the members of the group themselves, and will be supported by enthusiastic overseas Chinese friends who have friendship with the group at sea. As for the date and location of the founding meeting, and the procedures for filing with the local military and political authorities, etc., are currently being actively carried out.

Request to Build New-Style Slaughterhouses 128

Suggestions from the Commodity Inspection Bureau to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce

The annual value of China's livestock products and by-products is about 200 million yuan. Recently, various countries have used the excuse that China's livestock has not been inspected before and after slaughter to ban imports, causing significant losses to domestic merchants. For example, the United Kingdom prohibits the import of Chinese lard, and the United States requires disinfection procedures upon entry for Chinese casings and prohibits the import of Chinese ham and sausages. All of these factors negatively impact Chinese livestock products and by-products in international trade. Although the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has now established inspection bureaus in important locations, it has not been able to fully achieve the goal of having the United Kingdom, the United States, and other countries cancel these bans. The reason is that new-style slaughterhouses have not been established in various provinces and counties in China, making it impossible to provide effective proof of inspection before and after slaughter. From 1879 to 1891, the United States also faced similar pressure when exporting these products to Europe. Subsequently, the US government established a bureau for inspection, provided certification, built slaughterhouses in various states, and strictly implemented inspection before and after slaughter. European countries then lifted the bans one after another in 1891. China's current situation is very similar to that of the United States at that time. It may be possible to adopt its policies to adapt to the environment. The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau specifically requested the Ministry of Industry and Commerce on the 5th to consult the Ministry of Health and forward it to the special municipal governments and provincial governments with convenient transportation, first ordering the municipal and county governments along the railways to establish a relatively scaled new-style slaughterhouse in the city and county center within one year, implement inspection before and after slaughter, so that the United Kingdom, the United States, and other countries will no longer have any excuses. It is also requested that the Ministry of Education be consulted and forwarded to various universities with agricultural colleges to cultivate veterinary talents to meet the needs. The bureau also stated that it has established a livestock product and by-product inspection office within the bureau. Within the scope of its work, in order to prepare for promoting the realization of this matter, it has specifically sent Wu Deming, a technician of the bureau, to Hangzhou, Jiaxing, Wukang, Songjiang, and other places to investigate whether slaughterhouses have been established and the number of livestock slaughtered daily in each county for reference.

Local News 2

Beloved Son Buried Alive by Enemy 130

Thirteen-Year-Old Son Tragically Murdered

Nephew Went to Deliver a Message and Never Returned

Guan Liukun, a local resident, 43 years old, lives in Guan Lane, Tanzi Bay, and earns a living by growing vegetables. He has two children, a daughter who is 19 years old and unmarried, and a son, Mao Da, who is 13 years old and helps his father irrigate the garden. As the only son, Liukun loves him very much. At about 1 PM the day before yesterday, Mao Da went out alone, without saying where he was going. As evening approached, he had not returned home. His father became very suspicious and searched everywhere, but to no avail. Yesterday morning, Liukun ran to his sister, Hou Guanshi, but she had no clue either. It was not until about 3 PM that Hou Guanshi went to look at the wheat in the fields near the Yushi River near her residence. Suddenly, she saw a pile of soil next to the grave of her in-laws. She approached and saw that the ground had been dug up. She found it very strange and took a shovel to dig it up. About a foot into the soil, a child's foot suddenly appeared in the soil, wearing blue cloth-bottomed shoes, which seemed to be what her nephew wore. She was shocked. She immediately ordered her third son, Genbao, to report to her brother, Guan Liukun. However, Genbao did not return after a meal. Hou was impatient and went to Liukun's house to deliver the message herself. To her surprise, she learned that Genbao had not gone to notify him, which was very strange. Soon after, Guan Liukun reported to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau Police Station, and the patrol leader, together with the 22nd Picture Land Guardian Renxin, Guan Liukun, Hou Guanshi, and others went to the wheat field on the Yushi River next to the Hou family's grave to excavate. At a depth of about four feet, a corpse appeared. Guan Liukun recognized that it was his son, Mao Da. He mourned over the corpse and cried uncontrollably. The dead child was wearing a blue cloth shirt and pants, floral socks, and blue cloth shoes. His head and face were swollen and purplish-red, likely due to being buried alive. After thinking about it, Guan Liukun felt that his nephew Genbao was suspected of having gone to deliver the message on his sister's order but never returned. Therefore, the police took Hou into custody at the Fourth District Public Security Bureau for questioning. Hou is 63 years old, lives in Houjia Gate, and has three sons: the eldest, Aibi; the second, Er'a; and the youngest, Genbao, who is on the run. However, Hou said to others that there was no old feud between the two families. If her son was the murderer in this case, it was difficult to understand why he would be so cruel.

How Strange 131

Master Yang Tries a Case

Dispute Arises from Property Division and Loss of Deeds

Woman Forced to Go to the Xiao Wang Temple

Whipped and Covered in Scars

Master Yang Also Imprisoned

In Zhoujia Bridge, about three miles west of Gaohang Town, Pudong, there is a farmer named Shen Hailin. The four brothers were dividing their property at home a few days ago when four field deeds disappeared. His elder brother, Shilin, strongly accused Hailin's wife, Xi Shi, of stealing them. Since she did not steal them, she firmly denied it. Shilin claimed that he had his own way. At about 11 PM that night, Hailin's wife was doing embroidery when Shilin suddenly broke into the door and said that if she did not steal the field deeds, she should go to the Xiao Wang Temple to swear before Master Yang. The woman had no choice but to go with him. When they arrived at the temple, two figures resembling yamen runners suddenly appeared and put iron chains around her neck without asking any questions. They forcibly dragged her into the temple. The monks in the temple heard the noise and came out to look, but they were driven into a small room behind the hall by these people. They ordered the woman to kneel before a man who claimed to be Master Yang. At this time, the woman knew that they were impostors, so she was not afraid. The man claiming to be Master Yang sat majestically in the hall, like a judge, insisting that the woman confess and ordering the fake yamen runners to whip her. Although the woman was covered in scars, she still firmly denied it. Seeing that their plan had failed, the group left in a clamor. The next day, the woman sued the Fifth Precinct of the Third District. As a result, the so-called Master Yang was imprisoned. After strict interrogation by the precinct, it was learned that Shilin was the mastermind. The criminals were then sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Brothers Embarrassed 132

Asking Older Sister for Help

Female Worker Encountered Robbers in Desolate Place

Gold Ring, Gold Bracelet, and Gold Buttons Stolen

Security Guard Injured While Capturing Robbers

One Robber Shot and Captured

Jin Genmei, a local woman, 20 years old, who used to work as a female worker in a yarn factory and lives near the Qinshi Yangdian in Pudong, was passing through Taiping Bridge, south of the Qichang Stockade, in Pudong the day before yesterday afternoon. The place was very desolate. Suddenly, two robbers emerged from under the bridge, one holding a sharp axe and the other holding a sharp knife, blocking her path. They said to Genmei, "Older sister, recently, the brothers have been very embarrassed, please help us." After saying this, they raised their axes and knives to scare her. Seeing this, Genmei looked around for help, but there was no one to help her. She was robbed of a gold ring, a gold bracelet, and a gold button. After robbing her, they fled. Genmei immediately called for help. Yao Changsheng, a plainclothes security guard of the Third Team of the Qichang Stockade, happened to pass by and came running after hearing the call. Seeing the two robbers running away, he chased after them. The robber with the knife was slow in running, so he was caught by the security guard. The robber immediately turned around and stabbed the security guard in the face with the knife, piercing both cheeks and causing blood to gush out. After being injured, the security guard immediately drew his pistol and fired three shots. Two bullets missed, but the third bullet hit the robber's leg. He was injured and fell to the ground. At this time, more security guards came running after hearing the alarm and captured the injured robber. He was taken to the team. Since the injured security guard's injuries were quite severe, he was immediately sent to the Pudong Hospital for treatment. The captured robber confessed that his name was Fu Genfa, 21 years old, from Pudong, living at 34 Qichang Stockade. He had previously committed a crime in the public concession and was imprisoned for two years and six months. He was released in April of this year. His accomplice, Lu Jinquan, lived at 33 Qichang Stockade. According to the confession, the team sent more security guards to arrest Lu at his address, where he was captured under the bed in his bedroom. He confessed that he was 27 years old, a local resident, and had robbed Zhang Qigen, a security guard from Zhangjia Building, of a woolen overcoat, a watch, and four pairs of shoes in the same place last Friday afternoon. Later, he met a person in the same place, who had no valuables, so he only took a top hat and pawned it at a pawnshop in Yangshupu for one yuan. The team then took the stolen goods from the robbery of Zhang Qigen from Lu's house and checked them. Only one shoe was missing. That night, the two robbers were escorted to the Third District Police Station. After questioning by the district chief, they were sent to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Husband Did Not Return for Many Days 133

Woman Suspected and Took Poison

Usually, They Were Very Affectionate

One Day, a Big Argument Erupted

Liu Could Not Defend Himself

Taking Poison, Life in Danger

Liang Jiazhen, a Cantonese woman, 28 years old, living at 1633 Taoyuanfang, North Henan Road, because her lover, Liu, had not returned home for many days, suspected that he was having an affair. Yesterday morning, they had a disagreement, which led to her swallowing tranquilizer in an attempt to end her life. Her breath was weak, and her life was in danger. The details are recorded below:

Fallen into the Pits of Pleasure

Jiazhen was very intelligent as a child. She studied in school in her hometown for several years, so she can understand ordinary words. Later, her parents died, and the family's situation deteriorated. She was brought to Shanghai by someone and entered the world of pleasure, making a living by selling laughter. Because of her beauty and gentleness, many young masters were happy to associate with her. There were many who fell at her feet.

Married to a Desirable Man

Four years ago, she met Liu, a fellow villager. Liu is now employed at Juchanghe Food Store on North Sichuan Road. He is a young and dashing, handsome young man. They fell in love and soon made a lifelong agreement. After leaving the pits of pleasure, they built a love nest in a building at 1633 Taoyuanfang, North Henan Road. They were like a loving couple. For several years, they lived in peace.

Mother and Wife Came to Shanghai

However, Liu's hometown still has parents and a wife. After several years, he returned home to visit his relatives. Although letters were often exchanged, the elders longed for him. Last month, Liu's mother and wife came to Shanghai by boat and stayed at the Wan Hotel. The family was reunited, and they were very happy.

Mother Sick in the Hotel

Soon after, Liu's mother fell ill in the hotel due to acclimatization. Liu was naturally filial. In addition to going to work during the day, he returned to hire a doctor to treat her and take care of her, day and night. For a week, he did not take off his clothes. In the past two days, Liu's mother's illness has improved.

Tranquilizer

Because of this, Liu had not been to Liang's place for ten days. The night before, he returned home alone. After Liang met him, she vented her anger, saying that he had not returned for many days and must have a lover outside. Although Liu repeatedly explained the cause, Jiazhen did not understand. The argument continued all night. The next morning, at about 8 AM, Liu was about to go to work when he was stopped by Liang. A quarrel broke out, and it continued until about 11 AM. Liang took out a bottle of tranquilizer from the drawer and slowly swallowed it in front of Liu. At the time, Liu was angry and did not stop her. Suddenly, he saw Jiazhen's face turn pale, and she began to moan. He quickly sent her to Tongren Hospital for treatment by car. According to the doctor, she had taken too much poison, and her life was in danger.

Young Woman Wang Jinyuan 134

Committed Suicide at Home Late at Night

28-Year-Old Committed Suicide by Taking Opium

Family Said the Deceased Knew the Truth

Wang Jinyuan, a young woman from Changzhou, 28 years old, lived at 34 Mingxing Lane, Yinghua Street, Great Malu, and lived with her parents. She was quite free. In the age of modern social interaction, Jinyuan often went out to socialize. Unexpectedly, at about 1 AM yesterday morning, Jinyuan swallowed about two doses of opium paste for some reason. She was restless, and the maid found out and immediately told her mother. She reported to the Old Gate Patrol Room, which sent Detective Zhang Yi to investigate Wang's home. He saw Jinyuan lying on a brass bed, staring blankly. He realized that she had taken a lot of poison. She was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment in a detective car. Letter of Inquiry from the County Reorganization Committee 140

Regarding the Bail of Local Bully Liu Junfu

The Shanghai County Party Affairs Reorganization Committee sent a letter to the Shanghai Local Court yesterday, stating: "Regarding the case of Liu Junfu, a local bully from the Hua Jing Township of the Second District of Shanghai County, who was previously reported by the Second District Executive Committee for extorting the villager Chen Xinci, which was verified by our committee's investigation and referred to the county government for the detention of the said local bully to be punished according to law, it has been many days without a reply. We have now learned that the said local bully has been released on bail midway, causing strong indignation among the local citizens, who have repeatedly petitioned our committee for strict action. Therefore, we hereby send this letter to your esteemed court, requesting that the said local bully be promptly brought to justice to uphold the law, and that the details of the bail and the results of the handling be reported to our committee. We remain in public amity."

Special District Local Court 141

First Investigative Hearing

Zheng Xiaobao and Tang Meiquan from Wuxi broke into room 129 of the Huizhong Hotel on Hankou Road at 11:30 pm on March 9, robbing Chen Yeqiao and others of $240 in cash, and fled with the stolen goods. Chen immediately gave chase and apprehended Tang Meiquan. Although Zheng Xiaobao was blocked by the police who were alerted, he continued to flee. The police fired a shot, wounding his foot, and he was captured. The next morning, they were sent to the former Provisional Court, where the police department filed charges of robbery. However, Zheng and Tang claimed it was due to a gambling dispute. On the same day, Changren Ji Geng brought a set of dominoes and a dice shaker to testify, stating that he visited Zheng Xiaobao that night and saw them fighting. The room contained a set of dominoes and dice, which he took and gave to Zheng's mother to prove that the dispute arose from gambling. However, the plaintiff, Chen Yeqiao, insisted that this was not the case. The hotel tea servant was also summoned to testify that there were no gambling tools in room 229, and he had not seen Zhou at the hotel that night. The presiding judge, Sun Yuan, determined that Zheng and Tang were guilty of robbery and sentenced them to three years and six months of imprisonment. The witness Zhou Jigeng was handed over to the police for investigation into whether his testimony was false. Subsequently, on April 1, the Provisional Court was reorganized into the Special District Local Court. The internal organization of the court was different from before, so the police department requested the Special District Local Court to interrogate Zhou. The presiding judge then re-referred the case to the Prosecutor's Office for investigation. Chief Prosecutor Zhou Xianjue assigned Prosecutor Guo Huaipu to handle the case. Prosecutor Guo then gathered the case files, began to proceed, and specially opened an investigative hearing yesterday afternoon, summoning the plaintiffs Chen Yeqiao and Chen Gennian, father and son, and the Huizhong tea servant and the Chinese police who made the arrest to court. Zhou Jigeng was brought to the court for questioning. At the end of the investigation, it was determined that Zhou Jigeng was suspected of perjury, and he was ordered to remain in custody while the others were dismissed, awaiting indictment. Since the establishment of the Special District Local Court, although a Prosecutor's Office has also been set up, it is restricted by the agreement, and the prosecutors have not been able to fully exercise their duties. Therefore, although it has been more than a month since its establishment, this is the first case in which a prosecutor has independently opened a hearing to investigate and preliminarily try a case.

Western Woman Injured by Car 142

Sues for Over Six Thousand Dollars

The Western woman, Gao Ge, was hit and injured by a car driven by the driver Xu A'er in the Baochang Road area of the French Concession last month. The Western woman hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the French court, requesting compensation for the losses. The lawyer for the plaintiff stated that the plaintiff was admitted to the hospital for treatment after being hit on March 12 and has not yet recovered. The plaintiff could earn four or five hundred dollars a month from her business. Since the accident, she has suffered great mental trauma and requested compensation for losses and medical expenses, totaling six thousand four hundred and ninety-five dollars. The Chinese and Western officials ordered them to withdraw and await judgment.

Two Women 143

Involved in a Public Debt Dispute

Trial Reconciliation Attempted, Hearing Adjourned

The woman Bai Pan, who is quite wealthy, regularly buys and sells public bonds in the public bond market. Her counterpart is also a woman named Lin Aijin. Due to a dispute over the transaction of relief funds, Bai Pan hired lawyer Shen Yuesheng to sue Lin Aijin in the Special District Local Court for owing several thousand dollars. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou opened a hearing to examine the case. The plaintiff stated the dispute over the relief funds and amended the amount requested to be repaid by the defendant to three thousand nine hundred and seventy-eight dollars and fifty cents. The defendant hired lawyer Qu Yue to defend. After questioning, Judge Zhou advised both parties to attempt reconciliation outside the court. The case was adjourned to May 21st for continued hearing, and the plaintiff was instructed to invite the three witnesses to court at the next hearing. The defendant should also present any counter-evidence for review.

Xiamen Steamer Uncovers Trafficking Case 144

Two Children Rescued

The trafficker Cai Chen, a 39-year-old woman from Changxing, Zhejiang, recently lured two boys to Shanghai and boarded the Xiamen-bound Jinan steamer yesterday morning around 5:00 am, intending to sell them in Xiamen. As the ship was about to set sail, two investigators from the Women and Children Relief Association boarded the ship to inspect. When they questioned Cai, her answers were incoherent and untrue. They took Cai and the two children to the water police station. According to Cai, one of the boys was Cai Baosheng from Shaoxing, 12 years old, and the other was Xu Guisheng from Pengjiaqiao, 9 years old. She admitted that Cai was her son and was going to live in Xiamen. According to the two boys, one was Zhao Guisheng from Hunan and the other was Zhang Liansheng from Huzhou, which completely contradicted Cai's statements regarding their names and origins. As the case involved the inhuman trafficking of children for export, they were sent to the Local Court yesterday afternoon for disposition.

Kidnapping Case in Room 13 145

Shi Zhengcai Reports to District Investigation

Hengyi Inn Accountant Obstructs

Shoes and Clothes Under the Bed

Talking and Laughing in Room 18

The First District Headquarters in Nanshi received a report from Shi Zhengcai, a 31-year-old from Haimen, who works as a partner in a cigarette paper shop in the French Concession. He said that he received a letter from his family stating that his sister, Shi Youxian, had been lured to Shanghai by her sister, Han Shi, and her brother-in-law, Han Huaiyi, and hidden without a trace, with the intention of selling her. He was asked to find her in Shanghai. He and his relative Shi Jianglang carefully searched and learned that they were hiding in the Hengyi Inn at No. 29 Yanmatou Lane, 16th Shop, under his jurisdiction. He requested that the police be sent to arrest them. The request was approved, and detectives Dong Mingde, Yuan Haishan, Yu Maolong, etc., went to arrest them at around 6:00 pm. They inspected the guest register of the inn and found that they were staying in Room 13. They went to check the room, but no one was inside when they pushed open the door. They asked the inn servant, who said that the guests had gone out today. They further questioned Chen Jixun, the accountant from Haimen, who also said that they were not there. Suspecting that they were being evasive, they thoroughly searched the room and found shoes and clothes under the bed. They then asked the tea servant why there were these items in the room if there were no guests staying there. The tea servant remained silent. Suspecting even more, they searched all the rooms and found Han Huaiyi, his wife Shi, and her younger sister Shi Youxian sitting on the bed talking and laughing in Room 18. They were immediately arrested. The inn was accused of harboring and concealing the kidnapping of witnesses, and obstructing the investigation when the incident was discovered. Chen Jixun, the inn's accountant, was also brought back to the district for preliminary review by District Chief Chen, as he was clearly involved in the case.

Pudong Boat 146

Robbed in Lujiazui

Tang Shigen's Pudong boat was loaded with flour, soybean oil, and other goods from Dingshun and other shops, as well as more than a dozen male and female passengers, and set sail for Xinchang yesterday. The tide rose in the afternoon, and it set anchor. Around 7:00 pm, it sailed near Lujiazui. It was already dark, and two small boats sailed head-on. Tang, fearing a collision, steered to avoid them. Unexpectedly, the two boats surrounded the boat from the left and right, shining electric torches. They asked Tang where he was going. Tang, not suspecting thieves, replied that he was carrying passengers and goods. The thieves swarmed onto the boat, wielding iron rods or large knives, and rushed into the cabin, threatening the passengers and preventing them from making noise. They searched everyone, and none of the male or female passengers were spared. All the silver dollars were robbed. They then searched the stern of the boat, robbing Tang's leather box, which contained two hundred dollars in entrusted money and freight bills from various merchants. Before leaving, they smashed the rudder of Tang's boat, fearing that they would be followed, making it impossible for him to sail. When searching the passengers, a certain Ju, who was carrying boiling water, resisted and was stabbed in the arm. Tang hired a boat to unload the goods and sailed away after repairing the boat.

Fire on Shanghai-Hangzhou Train 147

At 10:20 am yesterday, the 21st freight train from Zhakou to Shanghai on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, while passing near Chang'an Station, caught fire in a connecting carriage No. 3429, which was fully loaded with tea and hemp sacks. The fire was very fierce. Fortunately, the conductor noticed it and immediately ordered the driver to stop the train. Together with the road police escorting the train, they worked hard to put out the fire, which was extinguished. Several tea sacks were burned, but the carriages were not damaged. The carriage was detached at Chang'an Station, unloaded, and reloaded onto another train to Shanghai. Therefore, the freight train arrived at the Shanghai station behind schedule.

Fire at Samsung Yarn Factory 148

At 10:45 am yesterday, the gatehouse of the Yongan Workshop inside the fence on the west side of the Samsung Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Road caught fire due to the carelessness of the person in charge of the pavilion while cooking. The fire spread to the wood, and the flames were raging. Fortunately, the fire brigade heard the alarm and drove to the scene to extinguish the fire. However, the gatehouse was completely burned. The estimated loss of the burned buildings and materials was several hundred dollars.

Bandit Arrested on Rue de Baler 149

Around 2:00 pm yesterday, the Shanghai Public Security Bureau sent a detective to the French Police to report that several bandits were hiding in a house at No. 2 Rue de Baler. The police chief immediately ordered a detective to go with them. They arrested a Hunan man named Liu Deqing in the house and took him to the police station. After a brief interrogation by the police chief, he was handed over to the detective to investigate the case.

Young Woman Accuses Husband 150

Of Bigamy and Abandonment

Wu Fuzhen, a young woman, recently filed a complaint with the Prosecutor's Office of the Local Court, accusing her husband Gao Jinshen of bigamy and abandonment. Her statement was as follows: On the tenth day of the tenth month of last year, she married Gao Jinshen, a partner in the Jushun Bean and Wheat Shop on Doushi Street, South Shanghai, with Chen Jiaxin and Jian Yi as matchmakers. The wedding was held at the China Hotel on Second Road. They immediately began to live together. Now, the defendant has abandoned her, and it has been discovered that the defendant is originally from Jiading and has a wife named Wu. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit for bigamy, requesting legal action. The court ordered Gao to be brought to court for questioning and detention, as the defendant had committed the crime under Article 254 of the Criminal Law. The public prosecution was filed. Yesterday morning, the Criminal Court, presided over by Shen Bingrong, specially opened the first court for trial. The plaintiff was absent. The defendant, Shang Jinshen, testified that Wu Fuzhen was introduced as a concubine by Chen Jiaxin last year, and that he still had a second wife, Wu, at home. At this point, the defendant's lawyer, Ye Fukan, rose and said that the defendant's wife, Gao Wu, was present in the gallery and requested that the court summon her to clarify the truth. Judge Shen then ordered Gao Wu to leave the gallery and asked the defendant, "Since you said you were taking a concubine, do you have any written evidence?" He replied, "Yes, but they stole it." He asked, "Was the wedding held at the China Hotel?" He replied, "There was no wedding. Moreover, Wu Fuzhen and the matchmakers came to the hotel by rickshaw." He asked, "Was the hall rented?" He replied, "No." He asked, "Which room was it?" He replied, "I don't remember, about a dozen." He asked, "Was a banquet prepared?" He replied, "No, please investigate." Judge Shen obtained the testimony and then ordered Gao Wu to the case to testify. She was 25 years old, from Luodian, and lived at Shenjiaqiao, north of Luodian. "Gao Jinshen is my husband. I have been married for three years as his second wife." He asked, "Have you had any children?" She replied, "I have a hidden illness and cannot have children, so I told my husband to take a concubine." He asked, "Was the wedding held in the hotel?" She replied, "I was tricked." He asked, "When your husband came home, did he tell you about marrying Wu?" She replied, "He (referring to Gao Jinshen) didn't tell me." Judge Shen said, "Then your husband hid it from you?" She replied, "I told him to marry her. I told him to live with me, but she refused." The judge obtained the testimony. As the plaintiff was not present, the case still needed to be investigated. He ordered that no debate be held and that another date be set for further review and decision. The defendant was returned to custody.

Rascal Attempts Theft, Fantasizes 151

The rascal Li A'da checked into a room at the inn opened by Chen Minghan on Minguo Road in the French Concession the night before. Li took apart the bedsheet and wrapped it around his body, hoping to escape. He was discovered by the innkeeper, who called the police. The police arrested Li and the stolen goods and took him to the police station. Yesterday, he was sent to the French court for investigation. The plaintiff first complained about the previous situation. Li A'da admitted that he was poor and had no choice but to steal. The French official sentenced Li to seven days of imprisonment as a warning, and the stolen goods were returned to the plaintiff.

Prostitute Dies for Love, Pitiful 152

Zhang Zhiyuan's Gambling Harms People

Sent Back to His Hometown After Recovery

Zhang Zhiyuan from Hangzhou was fired from his job because of his gambling addiction. He and his beloved prostitute, Zhang Jinbao, temporarily resided in room 30 of the Xin Su Hotel on Fuzhou Road. The previous evening, they bought opium and both took poison. The next morning, the tea servant discovered them and sent them to the hospital. Jinbao took more poison and died shortly after. The case was reported in yesterday's newspaper. The police in charge have taken the body to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Guo, a judge from the Special District Local Court, was appointed to inspect the body at the office. The public case was announced, and the Western police chief reported the results of the investigation after the incident, stating that Zhang lost his job and continued to gamble. The last gambling money of fifty dollars was moved by Jinbao for him, but he still lost. Zhang felt ashamed and took poison. Fortunately, he was still curable. It was requested that Zhang be sent back to his hometown after he recovered, as he was afraid that he would commit suicide again in Shanghai. As for the deceased Zhang Jinbao, no relatives were found. The Prosecutor ordered that Zhang Jinbao's body be handed over to Pushan Mountain Villa for collection. This prostitute can be said to have been single-minded. Unfortunately, she did not have discerning eyes and could not find a promising person in the world of prostitution to devote herself to.

Shen Zixiang's Act of Injury 153

Forensic Examination of Wu Bensong's Body

Wu Bensong, a vagrant from Huizhou, 31 years old, was taken in by the Zhabei Songhu Reformatory. He was beaten by the reformatory staff member Shen Zixiang with a stick the other day, resulting in injuries. The next day, Wu died. The director of the reformatory suspected Shen of murder, so he sent a piece to the Fifth District Police Station for detention. The guarantor reported to the Local Court and sent someone to examine the body. The deceased had wounds on his head and buttocks, but they were not fatal. There were also reasons for illness. After the family prepared the coffin, the police station, believing that the deceased did not die from injuries, but that Shen Zixiang's act of injury could not be avoided, transferred Shen to the Local Court yesterday for punishment.

Second Meeting of the Cholera Prevention Propaganda Committee 154

In order to curb the cholera disease, which is most likely to prevail in the summer and autumn seasons every year, the Municipal Health Bureau has specially joined forces with the Municipal Party Department, the Social Affairs Bureau, the Public Security Bureau, the Education Bureau, and other agencies to form a Cholera Prevention Injection Propaganda Committee. The Municipal Party Department sent Shui ZeKe and Zhang Yunqing. The Social Affairs Bureau sent Chen Leng and Seng Guo Yongxi. The Public Security Bureau sent Huang Jingzhi and Chen Timin. The Education Bureau sent Wang Keyong and Chen Shizhong. The Health Bureau sent You Jihua, Yang Xiling, Ge Sen, and others as committee members. They decided to assume responsibility for the publicity and supervision methods. The Municipal Party Department was responsible for the industrial and commercial groups, the Social Affairs Bureau was responsible for the industrial and commercial groups and charity groups, the Public Security Bureau was responsible for the shantytown groups, the Education Bureau was responsible for the school groups, and the Health Bureau was responsible for the party, government, military, and police groups. The implementation of the injections was handled by the Health Bureau, and the respective agencies were responsible for publicity and supervision. The second committee meeting was held yesterday, and it was decided to expand the propaganda methods and send letters to various newspapers, requesting that news about epidemic prevention be disclosed as much as possible, so that citizens can be alarmed at any time and know what to guard against, so as to prevent the breeding of epidemics and increase the people's knowledge of hygiene.

Closed Cases of Chinese and Foreign Appeals

A Total of More Than One Hundred and Twenty Cases

Chen Shiguang, the director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office, previously received instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding the outstanding cases of the Chinese and Foreign Civil Appeals Office attached to the former Diplomatic Office, ordering that they be transferred to the Second Branch of the Higher Court for acceptance.
