After receiving the order, Director Chen ordered the case manager Cheng Dahuan to collect more than one hundred and twenty cases from the cases that had been packed for transportation, so that he could write to the court and ask them to send someone to the office to accept them.

General Silk Cocoon Association 156

Regulations for Protecting the Cocoon Market

The General Silk Cocoon Association of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, considering the unrest in various regions, has drafted regulations for the protection of the cocoon market. These regulations have been submitted to the National Government and the provincial governments of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui for implementation. The submitted documents were previously reported. Now, the regulations for protecting the cocoon market are transcribed below:

Jiangsu Province (1) In all counties where cocoon businesses are located, the protection period is as follows: From May 20th to July 20th of the national calendar, a total of sixty days. This is the period for which cocoon merchants throughout the province request protection. The transportation of cash and cocoons depends entirely on the stationed troops, naval and land police in each area to provide appropriate protection at all times. If cocoon industry associations, cocoon directors, cocoon merchants, and Chinese and foreign merchants who come to buy cocoons need to request assistance from the military, public security bureaus, and county governments in these areas, it is requested that orders be issued to allow them to do so, so that officials and merchants can communicate without hindrance. (2) Protection matters are divided into five sections: (Section 1) The Dongting East and West Mountains of Wu County have traditionally transported cash from Shanghai by train to Suzhou. It is requested that four police patrol boats be dispatched to Suzhou Railway Station to wait for the arrival of cocoon merchants' cash and escort it, starting from May 20th. This will take about twenty days, ensuring the completion of transportation. For the subsequent twenty days, when dried cocoons are transported to Suzhou, they will be handed over in Suzhou or transported to other locations by train or boat for delivery. It is requested that protection be provided at all times. (Section 2) From May 20th to June 20th, these thirty days are the period for cocoon merchants in various counties, cities, towns, and villages to transport cash. At Suzhou, Wuxi, Henglin, Changzhou, Danyang, Zhenjiang, Nanjing, and Songjiang, Jinshan, Fengjing stations, as well as Changshu, Jiangyin, Jingjiang, Nantong, Haimen, Wujiang, and Pingwang ports, cash will be loaded and unloaded. It is requested that military and police be dispatched to take care of these locations. Where there are no military or police, county governments should assign guards to defend the stations and ports to prevent negligence. (Section 3) In cities, towns, and villages in Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Changzhou, Suzhou, Wuxi, Danyang, Yixing, Liyang, Jintan, Songjiang, Jinshan, Changshu, Jiangyin, Jingjiang, Nantong, Haimen, and other places, where banks and money shops are located during the cocoon market season, there will inevitably be cash inflows and outflows. It is requested that orders be given to the stationed troops, naval and land police, and county governments to maintain strict vigilance day and night. (Section 4) Wujiang and Wu counties are adjacent to Taihu Lake, and the areas along the way are critical. Chinese and foreign merchants travel by boat to the interior, passing through these areas day and night. It is requested that the naval and land military and police in these areas be notified in advance to provide protection at all times, and four police patrol boats be dispatched to patrol these areas from May 20th to June 20th, a period of thirty days. (Section 5) Police patrol boats are the most convenient. Historically, Chinese and foreign cocoon merchants have been able to follow behind the boats with their funds, which has been very helpful. This year, it is requested that the Chief of the Public Security Bureau inform the chiefs of each district bureau to instruct the patrol boats to select personnel suitable for the location and familiar with the situation and assign them nearby, starting from (May 20th). The allocations are as follows: 32 boats to the Huangpodun Wuxi Cocoon Industry Association, 20 boats to the Changzhou Wujin Cocoon Industry Association, 20 boats to the Daqinghong Jiangyin Cocoon Industry Association, 24 boats to the Xushezhen Yi Li Jin Cocoon Industry Association, 10 boats to the Fengjingzhen Song Jin Cocoon Industry Association, 4 boats to the Pingwangzhen Wujiang Cocoon Industry Association, and 10 boats to the Mudu Zhen Wu County Cocoon Industry Association. (Please consider allocating two boats nearby to be stationed in Guangfu Town.) The total number of police patrol boats is 120, which will be sent to each area to consult with the cocoon industry association and cocoon directors, and be stationed in various villages. Traditionally, cash has been transported from Shanghai to Wuxi and Changzhou stations, where it is unloaded and distributed to various counties via waterways. It is requested that each patrol boat escort the shipment to the villages for greater safety. Now, it is requested that the Chief of the Public Security Bureau select personnel suitable for the location and assign them nearby to understand the local situation and avoid unnecessary travel. Since the war, there have been many bandits in various places, and this year's cocoon market is unlike previous years. Only by requesting protection from local military and police through local cocoon directors and merchants can this be ensured. It is requested that this be communicated as well. (3) County governments and local military and police have always provided exceptional assistance in protecting cocoon merchants. This year is unlike previous years. It is requested that the magistrates of the cocoon-producing counties and the military and police be notified that from May 20th to July 20th, during these sixty days, when Chinese and foreign merchants come to the interior to purchase fresh cocoons, they should carefully protect the flow of money and goods, the transportation routes, and the locations where cocoon businesses store their funds. Chinese and foreign merchants will be deeply grateful. (4) Cocoon industry associations have been established in the cocoon-producing areas of various counties, with directors elected. In case of urgent public matters, they can consult with the county magistrate and military and police officers for handling. It is requested that consideration be given to the fact that fresh cocoons are only available for a few days, and there should be no delay in implementation. In a few places where associations have not yet been established, cocoon merchants who open cocoon businesses can directly apply to the Public Security Bureau and county government for protection. It is requested that a uniform order be issued for implementation. (5) In remote areas where there are no stationed troops or police, it is requested that the county government dispatch nearby military and police to protect them, or request the dispatch of police patrol boats to be stationed in key locations, to avoid being caught off guard and encountering danger. (6) During the cocoon market, goods have different qualities and prices fluctuate. Buying and selling are based on mutual agreement, and forced buying and selling are prohibited. If anyone uses cocoon sales as a pretext to gather a large number of people and forcibly buy cocoons at the cocoon businesses, it is requested that county magistrates be ordered to prohibit such actions and dispatch county police to be stationed in the cocoon businesses to strictly prevent disturbances by peddlers and local thugs in order to prevent incidents. The above items are submitted for implementation according to established practice. Any incomplete matters should be prepared by the cocoon industry associations of each county in a timely manner. In remote areas where associations have not been established, cocoon merchants can promptly request local officials to investigate and handle the matter to ensure thoroughness. (Attached list of cocoon-producing counties in Jiangsu Province) Wuxi County, Wujin County, Jiangyin County, Yixing County, Liyang County, Jintan County, Wu County, Wujiang County, Kunshan County, Taicang County, Jiading County, Baoshan County, Jingjiang County, Danyang County, Jiangning County, Yangzhou County, Dantu County, Jiangdu County, Yizheng County, Jurong County, Changshu County, Songjiang County, Jinshan County, Fengxian County, Shanghai County, Nantong County, Haimen County, Rugao County, Taixing County, Tai County, Huaiyin County, Shuyang County, Gaoyou County, Liuhe County, Baoying County, Siyang County, Lianshui County, Xinghua County, Suining County, Chongming County, Feng County.

Zhejiang Province (1) The most important thing for protecting Chinese and foreign cocoon merchants who come to the area to buy cocoons is cash. The routes and locations for transporting cash are listed below: Shaoxing, Shengxian, Xinchang, Shangyu, and other counties transport cash from Shanghai to Ningbo, where they change trains and transport it to Baiguan Town, Zhuji, and Xiaoshan. The above is transported from Hangzhou. Or, Shaoxing transports it to Yuyao, Cixi, and Fenghua. The above is transported from Ningbo. Yinxian, Hangxian, Linping, Haining, Jiaxing, Jiashan, Pinghu, Chongde, and Haiyan are transported from Shanghai. Or, it is transported from Hangzhou. Wuxing, Changxing, Anji, Wukang, Deqing, Xiaofeng, and other counties are transported from Huzhou or Hangzhou. (2) Protection period: Shaoxing, southwest villages of Shengxian, Shangyu, Zhuji, Xiaoshan, Hangxian, Linping, Haining, Yuhang, Xindeng, Fuyang, Changhua, Yuqian, Tonglu, Fenshui, Xinchang, northeast villages of Shengxian, Yuyao, Fenghua, Jiaxing, Jiashan, Pinghu, Chongde, Haiyan, Wuxing, Changxing, Anji, Wukang, Deqing, Xiaofeng, Yinxian, Cixi, and other counties: From May 5th to June 20th of the national calendar is the period for transporting cash. The packaging and transportation of dried cocoons to factories generally take place from May 10th to June 15th. This is the period for which cocoon merchants throughout the province request protection. It is requested that county governments, naval and land troops, and public security bureaus be instructed to provide appropriate protection at all times. (3) Protection matters are divided into four sections: (Section 1) Cocoon merchants transport cash from Shanghai to Ningbo, Yinxian, Cixi, and Fenghua, and then transfer it from Ningbo by train to Baiguan Town, where they unload and hire civilian boats to transport it to Shengxian, Xinchang, Shangyu, Shaoxing, and other counties. Cocoon businesses are located along the way in Zhangjiabu and Sanjie, where they unload. It is requested that the Ningbo local military and police be instructed to maintain order at the ports and stations and provide proper escort during unloading, loading, and along the way. From Baiguan Town, boats are hired to transport it to Zhangjiabu, Sanjie, Shengxian, and other places. Cocoon merchants should go to the military commander in the town to request that troops be dispatched for escort. It is also requested that the commander of the troops in the area be instructed to approve and implement any requests for protection from cocoon merchants immediately. (Section 2) Cocoon merchants transport cash from Shanghai to Hangzhou and then distribute it from Hangzhou to Xiaoshan, Zhuji, Tonglu, Fenshui, Fuyang, Changhua, Yuqian, Xindeng, Yuhang, Haining, Haiyan, Linping, Jiaxing, Jiashan, Pinghu, Chongde, Wuxing, Changxing, Anji, Wukang, Deqing, and Xiaofeng counties. It is requested that troops be assigned to be stationed in each county and that military and police in and out of the provincial capital's stations, Zhakou, and Gongchen Bridge and other ports work together to provide protection at all times. It is also requested that each battalion and bureau be instructed to approve requests from cocoon merchants for troops to escort them along the way and to return to camp to cancel their duties immediately after delivery. The travel expenses should be paid by the cocoon merchants to avoid delays caused by temporary applications for approval and dispatch. (Section 3) This year, cocoon funds for the Shaoxing area will first be gathered in Shaoxing City. If banknotes can be used, the day of departure from Shaoxing should be notified in advance, and the troops stationed in Shengxian should send a team to Shaoxing to meet and escort them. Shaoxing City should also send a team to escort them. The same should be done for Xinchang and Zhuji. For other counties, one team should meet and one team should escort, following the same procedure. (Section 4) County governments and military and police in cocoon-producing counties, as well as old prefectural cities such as Jiahu, Ningshao, and other places where wheeled vehicles pass and where money shops and banks have cash transactions, are requested to instruct local officials to patrol strictly day and night to provide protection. (4) County magistrates and local military and police are responsible for providing protection. It is requested that the county governments and military and police be instructed that from May 5th to June 20th, when Chinese and foreign merchants are transporting cash and goods, they should carefully protect the transportation routes and the locations where cocoon businesses store their funds, day and night, as stated in Article 3. They will be grateful. (5) Cocoon industry associations have been established in cocoon-producing areas of each county. In case of urgent matters, the cocoon directors can consult with the county government or military and police commanders for implementation. In places where associations have not been established, cocoon merchants can directly negotiate. It is requested that orders be issued for uniform approval and implementation to avoid delays. (6) In remote areas where there are no military or police, it is requested that county governments investigate and dispatch police from the county to take care of the area. If there are not enough police, they can borrow them from neighboring counties or request them from the provincial government. Preparations must be made in advance to avoid confusion and danger. In places where troops are stationed, the county government should select a strategic location to borrow houses for accommodation to avoid difficulties for the locals. (7) Goods have different qualities and prices fluctuate. Buying and selling are based on mutual agreement, and forced buying and selling are prohibited. If anyone uses cocoon sales as a pretext to gather a large number of people and forcibly sell cocoons at the cocoon businesses, causing illegal acts, it is requested that county magistrates in cocoon-producing counties be ordered to prohibit such actions and dispatch police to be stationed in the cocoon businesses to maintain order and prevent incidents. It is requested that the above items be followed. If there are any incomplete matters, cocoon merchants and directors can promptly request local officials to approve and implement them for the sake of public convenience. (Attached list of cocoon-producing counties in Zhejiang Province) Hang County, Yuhang, Haining, Fuyang, Lin'an, Yinxian, Fenghua, Xindeng, Yuqian, Shangyu, Yuyao, Jiaxing, Jiashan, Haiyan, Chongde, Pinghu, Tongxiang, Wuxing, Changxing, Deqing, Wukang, Anji, Xiaofeng, Shaoxing, Xinchang, Xiaoshan, Shengxian, Zhuji, Fenshui, Tonglu, Lanxi, Yiwu, Cixi, Changhua.

Anhui Province (1) Cocoon businesses in various counties import and export silver and goods through Wuhu and Datong. From May 20th to June 20th of the national calendar is the period for transporting cash. From June 10th to August 10th is the period for exporting cocoons, a total of eighty days. This is the period for which cocoon merchants throughout the province request protection. It is requested that the naval and land troops and public security police in Wuhu and Datong be instructed to provide appropriate protection at all times. It is also requested that county governments be instructed to comply. (2) Protection is divided into five sections: (Section 1) It is requested that the officers of the stationed troops in Wuhu and Datong send troops to guard the lighters and ports. When ships arrive, the cash should be transferred to the lighters day and night for protection to avoid negligence. (Section 2) It is requested that the troops in Wuhu and Datong provide escort whenever cash is transported from the lighters to the money shops and banks on the shore. (Section 3) It is requested that the troops in Wuhu and Datong provide strict protection wherever cocoon businesses' cash is stored in money shops and banks. (Section 4) It is requested that the troops in Wuhu and Datong, if cocoon merchants transport cash from Wuhu and Datong to various counties, send troops to escort them at the request of the cocoon businesses, and return to camp to cancel their duties after delivery. (Section 5) It is requested that the troops in Wuhu and Datong, if local military and police in inland counties are insufficient to protect the cocoon businesses, approve requests from cocoon merchants for troops to be dispatched to protect them. (Statement) Cocoon merchants have now established the Datong Interior Cocoon Industry Association in Datong, the Wuhu Interior Cocoon Industry Association in Wuhu, the Ningxuan Cocoon Industry Branch in Xuancheng, the Jingnan Jingji Cocoon Industry Branch in Jingxian, the Guangjian Cocoon Industry Branch in Jianping County, the Cocoon Industry Association Preparatory Office in Tianchang County, the Cocoon Industry Branch in Dangtu County, the Gangui Cocoon Industry Branch in Datong, and the Qingyang Cocoon Industry Branch outside Qingyang County, and the Qingyang Cocoon Industry Association Branch Office in Mu Town. It is requested that the county governments and stationed troops be informed that if the cocoon industry associations or cocoon merchants in the counties, townships, and towns request the dispatch of troops for protection, they should be approved immediately without delay, regardless of the distance or the number of people. However, local conditions vary, and the scope of business is not uniform. Therefore, cocoon merchants have always submitted their own requests, with the number of troops requested ranging from more than ten to only four or six, and the locations to which they are dispatched also varying in distance. The delivery of gratuities will still be handled according to established practice. (3) Wuhu and Datong have stationed troops and naval and land police, and the defenses are very strict. During each cocoon market season, cocoon businesses established in the counties within the port request the dispatch of troops from Wuhu and Datong for escort. When cash arrives at the business, they are stationed there until the cocoon business is completed and they return to camp. When additional cash is added for the second time, they go to the camp again to request the dispatch of soldiers for escort, and they return to camp on the same day. The officials have made great efforts to maintain order, which is very thorough. However, for critical passes, the directors of the cocoon industry association may submit a separate letter requesting the dispatch of soldiers for defense. It is requested that this be implemented in advance. If the troops in Datong are insufficient, the military officers stationed in Datong should report to the provincial government to request that nearby troops be dispatched for protection to ensure completeness. (4) Cocoon-producing counties such as Qingyang, Guichi, Tongling, Jingxian, Ningguo, Nanling, Langxi, Xuancheng, Dangtu, Guangde, Tianchang, Jingde, Fanchang, Jixi, Quanjiao, Gantai, Fengtai, Jianping, and other eighteen counties are requested to notify each county in advance to provide strict protection, day and night, for cocoon merchants transporting silver and goods and cocoon businesses storing cash. If cocoon merchants request assistance in the county, it should be approved. (5) If cocoon merchants in Wuhu and Datong request to go to the interior to be stationed for protection, the county government should plan thoroughly and allocate them properly. As for whether each county has military and police and whether they are sufficient for protection, or whether it is necessary to borrow military and police from neighboring counties, or to allocate troops from Wuhu and Datong, each county government should request the approval of the provincial government for implementation to avoid temporary difficulties. (6) The cocoon market is short, and there are often people who use cocoon sales as a pretext to gather dozens of people and forcibly sell cocoons at the cocoon businesses, taking advantage of the situation to engage in illegal acts. This year, the silk industry does not accept sub-contracts and does not allow peddlers to sell cocoons, and follows the instructions issued by the Anhui Finance Department five years ago, using sixteen taels as one catty as the standard, and adding two taels per catty as cocoon wool and moth depreciation according to salt and tea regulations, without any distinction, to prevent disputes. It is requested that county magistrates in cocoon-producing counties select local police to be stationed in the cocoon businesses to maintain order and strictly correct any illegal acts to maintain security and avoid accidents. (7) Goods have different qualities and prices fluctuate. Buying and selling are based on mutual agreement, and forced buying and selling are prohibited. Non-industry personnel must not interfere forcibly. It is requested that county magistrates in cocoon-producing counties be ordered to comply. It is requested that the above items be implemented by the Wuhu and Datong battalion commanders, naval and land public security bureaus, and the county governments of the eighteen cocoon-producing counties. Rice Boat Crew's Wage Increase Movement 157

Rice boat crews in Shanghai, due to meager wages that cannot cover their expenses, have once again launched a movement to increase wages and demand that if they are injured or killed in robberies, the shipowners should bear all medical expenses and provide compensation. Yesterday, the crews of various boats in Shanghai discussed this matter at Yizhichun. Representatives from various gangs reported that some shipowners, after being requested, have agreed to increase wages, considering the crews' difficulties, or have already increased wages. However, some shipowners are unwilling to increase wages. After discussion, if they do not increase wages, the crews will request again and set a one-week deadline for a reply.

Robbery on Huanghe Road Last Night 161

At around 8 o'clock last night, four robbers suddenly came to the Gongmao Pawnshop on Huanghe Road in the French Concession, claiming to pawn items. Child Welfare Society Rescues an Abused Child 162

The China Child Welfare Association rescued Xia Lan, who was abused in the home of Li Zhenqing in Nanxiang, on the 14th of last month, as reported in various newspapers. The association has now rescued Lu Laiqiu, an adopted son of the Lu family, who owns a restaurant on Beikai'er Road in this city, who was severely abused by his adopted father. Lu Laiqiu is a Ningbo native, eleven years old. The owner of the Lu family restaurant originally loved this child as his own, but in the past few months, he indulged in gambling, which led to the restaurant's business declining and making it difficult to make a living. The couple agreed to blame Laiqiu. In addition to beating him with firewood sticks from time to time, they repeatedly tried to drown him in the Huangpu River. Fortunately, his adopted uncle (the restaurant owner's cousin) rescued him a month ago and temporarily placed him with Shi Dexing Box Factory on Zhoushan Road in Tilanqiao through the introduction of neighbor Wang Jinheng (from Chongming). After the association received a notification from the outside world yesterday, it sent caseworkers Wang Guanyi and Ding Bingnan to the place. In addition to adopting the child, they also planned to verify the facts of the abuse and file a lawsuit according to law. It happened that Song Shaohuai, a Chongming native, wanted to adopt him as his son. Because Song's family was small but his character kind, the association agreed to his request, issued a certificate, and at the same time, the Lu family, who abused the child, had left Shanghai a few days ago. The association also stated that since the abused person has escaped from the water and fire, it will not pursue the matter for the time being.

To the Editor: Regarding the news item in your esteemed newspaper of the 6th of this month, concerning the arrival of automatic telephone equipment in Shanghai, we wish to clarify that the automatic telephone equipment of said bureau was ordered by the Ministry of Communications from our company. All materials were shipped from our main factory in Chicago, USA, to Shanghai. Several batches have already arrived in Shanghai, and the remainder are being continuously shipped by sea. The statement that the equipment was ordered from the German Electric Company and has been shipped from Germany is inconsistent with the facts. Therefore, we are sending this special letter to request immediate correction. Respectfully, American Automatic Electric Company, 19.5.7.

Respectfully, Shui Jiaquan, Manager of Taichang Fish Company, May 7th.

Special Article

Xu Peikun's Gold-Expensive, Silver-Cheap Relief Plan (Continued) 166

The current non-causal reason for Donghui is that due to the lifting of the Japanese gold ban and the recovery of Donghui's gold parity, the Japanese yen is no longer an important factor in controlling our country's silver exchange rate. Although this does not mean that the Japanese yen has no impact on the fluctuation of gold and silver exchange rates. In my humble opinion, if our country's financial system is not reformed, the Japanese yen will still have great power when it gets the chance. As for what forces are controlling the rise and fall of the silver exchange rate today, the simple answer can be as follows:

(4) The position of London's standard silver price

Here, a preliminary question arises: what is the relationship between London's standard silver price and the Shanghai silver exchange rate? According to past experience, the Shanghai silver exchange rate often changes with the gold speculation of Donghui, which shows that London's standard silver price does not have much controlling power over the Shanghai silver exchange rate. At the same time, we can prove that the Shanghai silver exchange rate has great power over the standard silver price. This point seems close to a cyclical debate, but the phenomena of the original action and reaction do exist in fact. The author has studied the relationship between them by statistical methods (this article will be published as soon as the manuscript is completed), and the result is still as described above. Therefore, it can be said that London's standard silver price sometimes determines the Shanghai silver exchange rate and is sometimes determined by the Shanghai silver exchange rate. This is an extremely cautious statement.) In addition to the above-mentioned mutual relationship, the change in London's standard silver price is also affected by various other reasons. Among them, Donghui was once an important factor, because Donghui directly affects the silver exchange rate in Shanghai. Secondly, the silver prices in Bombay, New York and other places are another powerful factor. Therefore, from the perspective of silver as a commodity, observing the complexity of the price-influencing factors and the magnitude of its speculative nature, it is a fallacy to explain the pricing process with a supply and demand law. If it is said that London is the concentration point of various speculative forces, and the silver price is generated from this, this statement is similar to the author's hesitation to use the term "speculation" as the principle of London's standard silver pricing, but before carefully examining other theories, I do not want to directly regard speculation as a principle. If we forcibly apply the supply-demand law, the bank's decision will be at the point where the market supply curve and the market demand curve intersect, and China, as the only powerful silver-using country, will have a huge impact on the demand curve, and thus also have a huge impact on the silver price. (To be continued)

A Laughing Matter by Hai Ke

Criminal: Police Chief, how dare I bribe someone as upright as you? To do so would be an insult.

Police Chief: It's not like that. It depends on the amount of the bribe. If the amount is too small, then it would indeed be an insult.

A: Have you ever been lost in the woods?

B: Yes, I have. Luckily, the wind god helped me. Otherwise, I wouldn't have survived.

A: What happened?

B: I was proposing to my sweetheart. Just then, a strong wind blew and she didn't hear me. But you know how fierce she is usually.

Husband: Have you heard that the city authorities are going to build a museum here? All the city's antiquities will be collected there.

Wife: Really? In that case, there's a place for this hat and dress of mine.

Mother: Child, you're being so well-behaved today. You're a good child.

Son: Mother, it's all because you put me in these new clothes. And these new shoes are too tight.

Anecdotes from the Construction Exhibition (Proverb 4) 167

The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Construction has been established for three years. To commemorate this third anniversary, a first Construction Exhibition was held, displaying exhibits for seven days, to promote awareness and to enable the people to understand the benefits and true meaning of the province's construction efforts. The intention is excellent. There were more than three thousand exhibits, a dazzling array, beautiful and numerous. Although it rained on several days in Hangzhou, visitors were still very enthusiastic. They all gave good comments, saying that it could be compared with the West Lake Exposition. Here are some miscellaneous notes on what I saw and heard.

Zhang Jingjiang braved the rain to attend. The exhibition opened on May 1st. It drizzled in the morning, but provincial and local dignitaries all arrived together. Zhejiang Governor Zhang Jingjiang also braved the rain to come and respectfully read the will. Various dignitaries then gave speeches successively, praising the achievements of the Construction Department in the past and in this exhibition. Afterwards, Huo Baoshu, the acting director of the department, reported on everything. All were broadcast via radio to all directions. The meeting was solemn and grand. After a photograph and refreshments amid the melodious military music, the meeting dispersed.

The room was full of spring. In the evening, an entertainment gala was held in the opening ceremony hall. The programs were all performed by colleagues from the department and staff from affiliated organizations. There were Peking opera, dance, magic, etc. Huo also made a guest appearance, with both southern and northern tunes, each showing its charm. Huo was originally from Guangdong, but his Mandarin is also very fluent. His Peking opera was especially stable. The guests in the room were all very excited and applauded continuously. Later, a film explaining the invention of electric lights and radio was shown, which could increase people's scientific knowledge and was also very interesting for research.

Remarkable achievements. Since Acting Director Huo and Chief Secretary Lin have been keenly managing the department, everything is new. All kinds of things are displayed this time, and the achievements are remarkable. There are 29 affiliated organizations, divided into four groups: industry, commerce, agriculture, mining, water conservancy, and transportation, displaying them. The whole is shaped like the letter T. There are various types of charts, specimens, products, and photographs. From the entrance to the inner room, the order is well-arranged. And the special displays of the six sections of the department are particularly striking.

The lights are brilliant. The department has set up signs in the main streets, urging all walks of life to visit, and a gate tower was erected on the lakeside. At night, the light shines for ten miles. The spectators block the road. The atmosphere of political tutelage and construction fills Hangzhou.

Borrowing an Umbrella to Tour the Mountains by Mei Sheng

Record of Monkey Wine by Li Shiyuan 168

My county has many high mountains and ridges, with natural scenery. Behind White Tiger Mountain, the stone caves surround like a series of stars, where short-tailed monkeys (tails no more than an inch long) live. Monkeys are intelligent. Villagers often bring porcelain bottles of fresh fruit. Upon arrival, they unload them in a corner and pretend to nap beside the cave, acting like they are resting. The monkeys like to play. They always come out and grab everything away. The villagers secretly peek at their whereabouts and know where the monkeys live. More than a month later, they go again. First, they set off firecrackers near the cave several times. The monkeys are all startled and flee out of the cave. The villagers come forward leisurely and go straight into their den. The fruit from the past has been brewed into a rich and strong wine, filling a dozen bottles. They carry them away one by one. Those who are good at drinking all say that its taste is more mellow than any fine wine. I don't know what technique the monkeys use to make this fine wine.

Previously, this magazine published a travelogue by a certain gentleman, who strongly praised the scenery of Niushou Mountain, calling it the best in the new capital. The day after I arrived in Beijing, I accepted an invitation from my friend Mr. Zhang and went on a tour in a group. The impression was excellent. Here are some miscellaneous notes.

Niushou Mountain is only more than twenty li away from Beijing. The county chronicles say that it is forty li away, which is actually an exaggeration. It belongs to the jurisdiction of Jiangning County. It can be reached directly from Beijing by car or horse-drawn carriage. Our group consisted of four people and traveled by horse-drawn carriage. The horse was old and tired. The driver was also old and ignorant. When passing Shizigang, because the road on the hill was very steep, the driver pulled the horse to move forward. The horse did not obey. We got out of the car and pushed it from behind. Just as we pushed it to the middle of the hill, the horse suddenly slipped and retreated. We used all our strength to resist it. Fortunately, nothing happened.

After passing Shizigang and reaching Tiexinqiao, it suddenly rained. We were all very frustrated, but when we saw the green light along the road, the grass and flowers all showed signs of life. Inhale, and the smell is incomparably refreshing and handsome. Niushou Mountain also smiled at the welcoming people. I suddenly felt a surge of pride. When we arrived at the foot of Niushou Mountain, the needle of the watch had pointed to half past one. The rain became stronger. We lingered outside the door of the farmer's house and begged to borrow umbrellas. The villagers initially refused. They promised to pay rent, and then they got three umbrellas.

Zhang Gai moved forward and twisted about a mile. Then I got a mountain climbing path. At that time, the rain was less killing. The four mountains have been replaced by clouds. Looking up at the top of Niushou Mountain, a few laps around the cloud. Lightly swaying like smoke. Tower too. The building is also. The pavilion is also. If there is nothing. Seeing it is amazing. We bravely climbed the mountain and rested at Meian. The so-called Meian is Yumeihua Hall. The ancestral house is several columns, and Qingdao people are enshrined. The old man Shouci burned tea to feed us. I had a big meal of bread here. Very full.

Go to Pujue Temple from Yumeihua Hall. I can't find a monk anywhere. A mountain boy led us to the temple to view the pagoda, which is said to be a bat, pagoda. There is a small path beyond this to climb the mountain. Then I visited Guanyin Cave in order. Yinmachi. Tushita Palace. The nose of the bull is everywhere. All cannot be stayed. Only on the rock of abandoning one's body. Looking at the mountains facing each other. Wrapped in cloud floss. Occasionally open and close. Like a virgin peeping at people. Extremely charming. At that time, the rain line was dense again. We stood precariously with umbrellas and clothes were wet. And the heart is very happy.

On the way back, the wheels and axles were trapped under the bridge because something happened across the small bridge. It was so dangerous that I still feel frightened when I think about it. Zhang Jun said that this is the most memorable thing in the tour.

In the fifth second year of the Republic [1936], Master Zhang Yishan of Taizhou married off his third daughter, Shi Yun, again at the Central Grand Hotel. He first inquired about my family, then asked how many daughters Master Yishan had, and then asked about the new groom's family background and talent. I responded based on what I knew. Then, because Mrs. Zhang told me in detail about Master Yishan's sorrow for the times, and also about the disaster situation in Taizhou, Mr. Ziyu then vividly described everything about life in Huizhou. Hearing this, I suddenly realized that Huizhou was originally a major prefecture. Ziyu, who was usually engaged in salt transport, said that Huai salt is now in a desperate situation. Taxes and mortgages, and smuggling are rampant. The salt merchants have almost lost their capital. I said, "Huizhou is a large prefecture, and its commercial prosperity does not rely solely on the Huai salt industry." Ziyu frowned and said, "Whether it's tea, lacquer, or bamboo and wood, they are all Huizhou products, but now they are gone. Tea and red carpets

Another Yu Shuang in Female Roles Edited by Lu 170

Yu Shuang's stage name is known throughout the world. Those who have been personally taught or privately admire her are springing up everywhere. However, the mantle has been passed down to only one person in the North and South, namely Xin Yanqiu's name Yu Hua. When I was staying in Beiping [Beijing] in the past, when I was still an unknown actress, I and my old friend Mr. He Xiangya most appreciated her and believed that she was a Yu Shuang among female roles. Indeed, after she went south, her reputation grew day by day. Even old actors like Yang Xiaolou did not hesitate to lower themselves and were willing to act with her, showing a momentum of surpassing the blue and overwhelming Yu Shuang. It has been a long time since then, and I don't know how her skills have progressed. Recently, Wu Fengchun, a well-known teacher from Shanghai, came and said that he had a younger sister named Huang Yanlu, whose makeup and acting were very similar to Yu Shuang. Her face was delicate and beautiful, even more so than Yu Hua. She would be performing that day at the Postal Peking Opera Conference of the Shangzheng Association. He asked me to go and watch. I smiled and nodded, but didn't take it seriously. In the evening, Wu came again, so I went with him. Upon arriving at the meeting, Wu brought the beauty to see me. Her face was beautiful, just like Yu Hua. Her conversation was especially elegant and pleasing, even better than Yu Hua. The play performed that night was "Bao Lian Deng," co-starring with the famous amateur actor Wang Zhenbai. This gentleman's makeup was elegant and his voice was sweet and pleasant. His pronunciation and dialogue were especially clear and valuable. He is an old hand in this. New Method of Insulating Urban Noise by Lu Bing 171

I read in a previous column that the noise in New York City is enough to harm the health of residents and cause many cases of deafness. Urban noise is most prevalent in the United States, because there are many factories and streetcars, resulting in huge noise levels that can be heard everywhere, and there is almost no clean place. According to a recent issue of the American magazine, this kind of obnoxious noise has long attracted the attention of the scientific community. They want to invent an object that can absorb part or all of the noise so as not to disturb the eardrums. After many tests, they have found several substances that naturally have the above-mentioned effects. One of them has a particularly great ability to isolate noise, called EelGrass. This algae is produced on the coast of Newfoundland. Although it can also be collected elsewhere, the quantity is small. The method is to wash the algal leaves, dry them in the sun, and then use thick brown paper on both sides for insulation, adding extremely heavy pressure to make them firm and thick. If this creates a brick shape, take it to stack the surrounding walls, then people are in it. Outside the sound wave can be ignored. It is very difficult to collect and manufacture algal leaves. The price is also expensive. One more floor. People in the algae room can talk to each other. Because all sides can be absorbed. It is not easy to distinguish without shouting loudly. In fact, it is not an ear canal, but it is affected by algae and becomes hard of hearing. And to use it as a church classroom, etc. This algae room is even more unsuitable. Therefore, although scientists have successfully tested it, it has not been widely used in the United States.

It is recommended that people who study transportation have a copy. It is currently sold by the Minzhi Guangyi Bookstore for only four cents a copy. In addition, the Economic Weekly published by the association has reached its sixteenth issue. It is one of the few economic research publications in the country. One cent per issue. External postal delivery is available, and subscriptions are welcome. (Zhizheng)

Eleventh Episode: Cui Luo Zhu Qiao, Celebrated Ladies Return, Talented Scholars, Azure Houses, Crimson Curtains, Young Women Marry into High Society

Let's talk about this episode. It was Mei Lanfang's first time coming to Shanghai, so the longing of the Shanghai gentry women was very strong. Because at that time, he already had a reputation in Beijing. There were many people who supported him. He had a publicity department. Of course, it was close to people in the newspaper industry. This publicity department was out of a sincere heart and did not spend half a cent of funds. Compared to the publicity departments of other political parties, it was even more loyal. The loyal comrades of the Mei Party, and they were all contemporary writers. They wrote those articles to protect the party. Not only were they publicized in Beijing, but they also had to send the manuscripts to Shanghai newspapers for publicity. You all know that writing promotional articles has a lot to do with the quality of the article. People with poor writing skills, say it over and over again, just those few words, can't come up with anything new. Open your mouth and see your throat. It's as if as soon as you open your mouth, people know what you're going to say. Therefore, that kind of promotional text, as long as you read a few lines, people can't read it anymore. If you teach people with excellent writing skills to do propaganda work, they can come up with all kinds of ideas and turn out all kinds of tricks. If he wants to support someone, or if he doesn't support that person, he first criticizes many people. He also praises people who are not the goal, but with many shortcomings, not as good as a certain person, who is a complete talent and complete beauty. This is called the method of setting off the moon with clouds. Or it only discusses one kind of art, and does not focus on people, but only a certain person is the best at that kind of art. Fallen leaves return to their roots, and it is still for him to promote it. And the elegance of the writing and the brilliance of the strokes are all related. People see that his article is good. Even if they don't want to promote this person in their hearts, they unknowingly fall into the magic of his writing and publish it for him. Therefore, they even spread the famous sentences in the text. Isn't this a trick of cunning writers? There are many capable people in Mei Lanfang's party department, all of whom are writers and lyricists. In the city of Beijing, in the late Qing Dynasty, there were originally those officials of the Ci Cao Department, and it was a common practice to support actors. Since the so-called Eight Great Hutongs in recent years have declined from Yin to Yang, they have been completely occupied by those girls. It is difficult to get a talented person. There are also many who are unworthy of being supported. No matter how eloquently it is said, its original quality is nothing more than that. Or after putting on makeup, it is still passable. But after taking off the makeup, the cheekbones are high, the cheeks are protruding, the chest is upright, and the back is hunched. A vulgar appearance is also disappointing. Seeing is believing. In the end, you have to see it with your own eyes to be correct. Now, Mei Lanfang, after putting on makeup, is light and graceful, making people satisfied. He really is a woman. Even after taking off the makeup, he feels handsome and fresh. He is a beautiful man. Therefore, today, those people in the Mei Party first come out to show their faces when he is not wearing makeup.

Silkworm Ants Are Forming Cocoons in Large Numbers... Early Silkworms Will Be Shedding Cocoons Tomorrow

The silkworm flood in Zhejiang Province is earlier than that in Jiangsu Province, and the areas of Yuhang and Haining Chang'an in Hangzhou Province are earlier than Jiahu and other areas by four or five days. This year, the hatching of seeds in Hangzhou County and other places was earlier, but the climate was not good. At first, it was cold and hot, and then it was cold and rainy, which caused the silkworms to develop slowly, and silkworm farmers felt it difficult to raise them. Fortunately, most of the seeds are improved species, and officials are sent to guide and take care of them. Improved species have little loss, but local species have lost a lot after the third sleep until the major sleep in the bud leaves. Now the cocoons are forming in large numbers, and the early silkworms will be shedding cocoons tomorrow. The cocoon firms in Hangzhou County, Yuhang, Haining, Chang'an and other places are expected to be able to open the scales around the 10th.

First Batch of New Tea Has Already Been Shipped 183

Yesterday, the Italian Postal Shipping Company's ship, Venice, set sail, loaded with more than 200 boxes of new green tea purchased by British firms and shipped to Europe for sale. This is the first new tea product this year.

Food Rioting, Prices Soar Then Fall 184

Yesterday, about ten ships arrived at each stall in Zhabei, and the market sales were dull and unmoving. The trend of white japonica rice was still the same as the previous day. The overall trend was still high and then fell, so the medium and secondary japonica rice were subject to price cuts every day. Customers stopped taking delivery of goods priced above 17 yuan. Although the price was short, there was no intake. There were few arrivals and sales of thin rice, and the situation was depressed. The top goods were still actively sold, and the rest were soft. The mutton and dujian rice were also tired, because there were few customers and the goods were poor, and the influence of foreign rice could only follow the market and decline. The buying was weak and the bottom was still thick, so the market continued to be small.

Ships arrived at the Shanghai South River one after another, and the roads were smooth. Changshu and Xibei japonica rice improved, then fell again. The market was similar to the previous one. Su Tong white japonica rice sales were not moving, but high-priced rice was still welcomed by some customers, while secondary rice was not transacted, and the price was flat. The southern early rice had few arrivals and sales, but the market was not prosperous, and the market was also short. The mutton dujian rice was still mainly from Nanzhuang local towns, and there were few Tongli and Beizhuang. The sales were very light, and the market was stable and inconsistent, with ups and downs of about a few corners. The white yuan market was deserted, and the goods arriving recently were also barren. Most of the guest gangs are watching and waiting, only the local street is slightly entering, and the price is still mediocre.

Yesterday's foreign rice market stabilized. Northern Sales Are Active... Manufacturers Are Taking Delivery. Near and Far Leap... About Two Cents Yesterday, the flour market rose again and again in each month, especially the increase in this month. I have already said before what the key to this month is. The expiration and violent fall in the previous month was difficult to get rid of because customers could not afford it. When the price was opened this month, because the market fell miserably, the northern sales had been jointly planned for a long time, and Tianjin's reserves were not abundant, and the sales were very smooth. The need for Shanghai flour is not as indifferent as before. Taking advantage of this opportunity, a certain factory gradually took delivery of more than 100,000 bags this month, so those who know the inside story have long expected it to change. During the Qinghuang season, attention should be paid to actual sales. Considering the recent situation, it should be the first step to reach two liang and five qian. If the customers are still being drawn out, I am afraid there are two or three good degrees. As a result, this month has risen by two cents and seven li and a half from the previous day. The distant period has also risen sharply due to the reported rise of foreign wheat by five, six, seven, and eight corners. It is estimated that the June increase is two cents and a half, the July increase is one cent and seven li and a half, the August increase is one cent and a half, the September increase is two cents, and the October increase is one cent and a half.

Tales of World Literature (1) (4) (8) by American John Macy, translated by Hu Zhongchi 188

Chapter 38: Nineteenth-Century French Prose by Lanfaxi

Du De's friends, Edmond de Goncourt and his brother Jules, were leaders of the Naturalists, or more accurately, the Visualists. To them, life was not so much material for stories, but rather material for detailed descriptions like paintings. However, as Stevenson said, the typical French story of literature is superior to their theories. In several of their novels, if only one is mentioned, such as "Renée Mauperin," they combine the ancient art of storytelling with the meticulous analysis or impressionistic depiction of the inner workings of characters, which is somewhat new in their hands. More important than the novel is the "Diary," which is not only an expression of the author's beliefs and personality, but also a brilliant light shining on French literature of the 19th century. Edmond de Goncourt left property to establish the "Academy," initially a protest against the official French Academy, but now a generally recognized organization. Its supreme substantive award for literary achievement is coveted by all young French writers. It has always been a powerful force in French literature advocating freedom and courage.

Deeply influenced by Goncourt, but also going his own way with a strangely shaped fierce will and strength, is J.K. Huysmans. He began with realistic novels like "Marriage Life" as a follower of Zola, and ended with religious mysticism, such as "The Abbey." Only two or three of Huysmans' books have been adequately translated into English, or not at all. His richly colored prose is difficult to translate. He is clearly an author's author, a darling of literary people. However, he will surely become even more famous in France and other countries in the future.

A delicate artist whose beauty can be appreciated by all kinds of readers is Pierre Loti, who died in 1923. He was a naval officer who had seen much of the world and felt the magic of the sea and exotic lands. He skillfully and honestly reproduced his experiences and impressions in his novels and memoirs. In the South Seas, he saw "Loti's Marriage," in Japan, "Madame Chrysanthème," and on the Breton coast and the North Sea, "An Iceland Fisherman." He also infused his sensitive personality into external descriptions and events.

Loti is an Impressionist; in his view, the world is color, is sensation, and is an experience that has little to do with morality in the sense of good and evil, wherever it is found. Paul Bourget gradually inclined towards a conservative, moral view of life, a sharp, or rather, strict researcher of society. He delves into the hearts of the characters he portrays. If his attitude were less gentlemanly, it would strike our hearts. However, he is an artist, and "The Disciple" and "The Promised Land" are novels of first-rate value. Bourget and his era are somewhat harsh and overly realistic in their analysis, and conservative in their view of life. Before the Great War, there were young, but not necessarily immature, people who saw "life" in the light of a new idealism. The main figure among them was Romain Rolland, whose "Jean-Christophe" is an international novel with a German musician who gained some experience in France as its protagonist. Although it is infinitely long, it is widely read in France, and in its English translation. His spirit embraces the world, but the world embraced in 1914 became a death grip. Romain Rolland, in a booklet called "Above the Battle," strove to rise above it. For this booklet, and other humanitarian articles, he did not gain fame among the warring nations. Anatole France maintained the tranquility of the privileged old era. Henri Barbusse (in "Under Fire") and other writers made use of the war.

Looking at modern English and American literature, we see that it is impossible to point out what is being done or what is an influential movement. For someone who did not come into being within it, who did not live in it, it is much more difficult to evaluate, judge, or even know a work in that literature at a glance. Nevertheless, we can try to suggest, not as a prophecy, that the death of Marcel Proust marked the end of an era. His novel "Remembrance of Things Past" seems to be a meticulous study of modern society seen by a sensitive observer, the culmination of psychological novels over half a century, a summary of what already exists, and also a prelude to the unknown future of the novel.

In one department of literature, France occupies a supreme position: criticism. From Balo to Rémy de Gourmont and the young people of today, French criticism has always been creation in the highest sense, excellent in itself and for itself, and of immense value for its influence on other forms of literature. The school of Sainte-Beuve, Renan, Taine, and Scherer is still flourishing. Following the elder giants, Brunetière and Faguet, two scholars, appeared, as well as Anatole France, the greatest of the impressionistic critics. France is often a critic even in his novels. Two outstanding figures who died young are Marcel Schwob, who had a keen and knowledgeable interest in English literature almost as much as in French literature, and Émile Hennequin, whose extremely concise studies of French writers and even foreign writers such as Dickens as part of French literature can be regarded as the last word in the art of literary essays. In the department of criticism, the entire literary world bows to France.

Qingfeng Garden

Feast of Tastes 189

The palace mistresses are hosting a banquet.

In order to make the location suitable, the palace mistresses had to make do and chose a small restaurant near the school that was relatively clean to host the banquet. The time was 7:00 PM, when the dinner rush was about to end. Although the filthy little restaurant was empty, the messy tables and chairs and the cluttered cups and plates had not yet been cleaned up. The palace mistresses, fearing that the invited young masters would be hungry, urged the waiters to hurry up and clean up, while they themselves helped with the arrangements. The fragrance of sweat permeated from their clothes, mixing with the greasy air. Their disheveled hair became even more disheveled. After a burst of activity, the small restaurant actually took on a new look. The messy tables were put together to form a rectangular dining table, covered with a clean white tablecloth, and several pots of flowers and plants were placed in the middle. In this way, it was indeed much more beautiful.

In addition to the decorations, a delicate and exquisite name card was placed in front of each seat, so that the young masters could sit according to their assigned seats and not mess up the order pre-determined by the palace mistresses. The patterns on the name cards were made of colored ink splattered on them, which were very beautiful. It is said that these were specially made by the palace mistresses themselves, spending a lot of time. After everything was arranged, the hosts asked the waiters to invite the invited young masters, who were separated in another room, to take their seats. It turned out that the impatient young masters had arrived very early. The palace mistresses, fearing that standing beside them would be inconvenient for the arrangements, stuffed them all into another room to wait. At this time, the young masters were indeed as hungry as the palace mistresses had guessed, constantly looking at the clock and waiting until the waiter said the word "please," they all appeared one by one in the dining hall as if they were flying. They were all wearing Western suits, with stiff trouser legs, plus a very obvious and sharp pleat. Their waists and backs were stiff and straight. Although one or two of them were as thin as weasels and short, their spirit was extraordinary. They stretched their necks upward with force, almost hiding the shortcomings of their shortness. There was also one whose eyes were white and staring at a palace mistress with a smile. The palace mistresses also greeted them with smiles.

They took their seats and the dishes were served one after another. The hungry young masters all restrained their laughter and busied themselves moving their lips up and down, but they still couldn't cope with the chopsticks of food being sent from their hands. They didn't even have the leisure to distinguish the taste, because they were all secretly wondering how the stupid cook could cook such delicious dishes.

The palace mistresses remembered the entertainment they had prepared. Taking advantage of everyone burying their heads in their bowls, they quickly brought out the paper basket. The basket was filled with many paper strips folded into concentric knots. The paper strips were written with various actions and songs. They went around the seats and asked each person to pick one. After the young masters saw what was written on the paper strips, they were all a little hesitant to perform. However, how could they withstand the urging of the strict commander, the palace mistress? So laughter rose again. Laughing actions and ear-piercing songs were performed and sung one after another. Some kowtowed to the person opposite them, some imitated the cries of birds and beasts, some did somersaults on the ground, some...some...

In the midst of wild laughter, the young masters and palace mistresses dispersed. The silent road was suddenly filled with pleasant air. The moon was also very good at joining in the fun, emitting a different kind of light to illuminate the proud sons of heaven who were returning to the palace with an indescribable feeling of joy in their hearts.

The Construction of the Central University Auditorium 190

The news of the construction of the Central University Auditorium had been heard two years ago. However, it was initially a pie in the sky due to lack of funds. Last year, President Zhang re-proposed the discussion on Commemoration Day, and said that no matter what, construction would begin in February or March this year, and the building would be completed in six months. Therefore, the roar of building the auditorium unknowingly started again. At that time, we students were really overjoyed under this situation of "the mountain rain is about to come, the wind is filling the building."

Ah, our "overjoyed" emotions continued until March 28 this year, when the auditorium's construction project actually began. While this construction project has not yet been completed, let me talk about the various things related to the construction of the Central University Auditorium.

The current buildings on the campus of Central University all have concrete plans. When it was Dongda University, American designer Meng Fei was hired to design the entire school's drawings. The new additions are mostly built according to this drawing. The recent plan and drawings for the construction of the auditorium, of course, cannot escape the exception. In addition, the school's twelfth administrative meeting last semester resolved that a project construction audit committee must be established to discuss any construction of houses with a cost of more than 5,000 yuan. Therefore, this construction of the auditorium also followed this resolution. First, a project construction audit committee was organized, and President Zhang separately sent letters to hire Mao Xie, Lu Shusen, Liu Futai, Liu Duncun, Lin Pingyi, Yu Liji, Wang Mingzhi, Xue Shaoqing, Zhang Yiqiao, and Cha Xiaoxian as ten members of the Auditorium Construction Committee. However, when the project construction audit committee was organized the year before last, it was still in the era of the university district system, and the distribution of offices in the auditorium was prepared for the use of both the university headquarters and the Executive Yuan. Now that the university district system has been abolished and the Executive Yuan has ended, the offices have been changed, so the drawings of the auditorium have also been changed. According to President Zhang's report on the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Day on December 23 last year, the drawings of the auditorium are as follows:

"The location of the auditorium is at the end of Dazhong Road, opposite the main gate, that is, in front of the flat dormitory. The Science Hall is on its left, and the future Industrial Hall is on its right. The Biology Hall is in front of the Science Hall, and the Library is in front of the Industrial Hall. These five buildings stand side by side, and the auditorium is in the center, forming a situation where the springs and stars surround the North Star. In front of the auditorium, the corridors form a circle, in the middle of which is planned to build a bronze statue of Sun Yat-sen. The style of the auditorium adopts the ancient European style. The front corner tops and four round columns are in the Greek style, and the middle dome is in the Roman style. From bottom to top, it is 104 feet high. The top is made of copper with heat-insulating glass windows. Light is introduced into the auditorium through these glass windows. On both sides of the auditorium, the offices are on the left and the professors' lounge is on the right, with roof gardens above. The plane of the hall is octagonal, the podium is very large and can be used as a stage. There are also dressing rooms next to it. There are three floors inside. The second and third floors have boxes and offices. The third floor has a movie machine room. In total, the three floors can accommodate 2,500 people." (The above is from the Central University Daily on December 24, 1929).
